### p42_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Tasks to complete before using Cisco EPN Manager|For information, see:|
|---|---|
|Setup and configure the Cisco EPN Manager server.||
|Add devices to Cisco EPN Manager and create device<br>groups to simplify device and network management.|Add and Organize Devices, on page 31|
|Enable monitoring for interfaces and technologies used by<br>the network.|Monitor Device and Network Health and<br>Performance, on page 231|
|Customize alarm and event behavior for your deployment<br>(for example, alarm and event refresh rates, and e-mail and<br>trap receivers).|Set Alarm and Event Management Preferences,<br>on page 257|

## Page 43

### p43_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Get Started with Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager (Cisco EPN Manager)|Col2|
|---|---|
|**Use the Main Window Controls**||



### p43_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|The top left of|the Cisco EPN Manager title bar provides the following controls.|
|---|---|
||Menu button—Toggles the main Cisco EPN Manager navigation menu on the left (also called<br>the left sidebar menu)|
||Home button—Returns you to the home page (normally the Overview Dashboard)|



### p43_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Col1|Web GUI global settings—log out, change password, , adjust your GUI preferences, check<br>a Cisco.com support case, and so on.|
|---|---|
||Current Server Time—displays the current server time and date.|
||Online Help—launches the online help (User and Admin guide) for Cisco EPN Manager.|
||Refresh—refreshes the page.|
||Dock—opens a side dock window that displays your recent searches and navigational history.|



### p43_default_t4 (default, high confidence)

|Col1|Alarm Summary—Provides a visual count of alarms in the categories that you specify.<br>Clicking this area opens the Alarm Summary popup window.|
|---|---|

## Page 45

### p45_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Get Started with Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager (Cisco EPN Manager)|Col2|
|---|---|
|**Service Performance Dashboard Overview**||



### p45_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Performance > any of the tabs d|described in the following table.|
|---|---|
|**Dashboard Tab**|**Information Provided**|
|CEM|For the selected Circuit Emulation (CEM) circuit, the dashboard displays<br>details, such as<br>• name<br>• type<br>• creation date<br>• statistics (you can toggle between the statistics for the circuit's<br>endpoints)<br>• number of packets lost during transmission<br>• number of packets reordered in the jitter buffer before they reached<br>their destination<br>• number of jitter buffer overruns and underruns<br>• number of packets ordered incorrectly and subsequently dropped<br>• number of malformed packets<br>• number of seconds that were errored, severely errored, or unavailable<br>• failed events, and<br>• dashlets that chart the number of Explicit Pointer Adjustment Relay<br>counters (such L-bits and P-bits) that have been generated and received<br>**Note**<br>To view these dashlets, both the CEM and Pseudowire Emulation<br>Edge to Edge monitoring policies must be enabled. See Monitoring<br>Policies Reference, on page 985.|



### p45_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager 7.0 User and Administrator Guide|Col2|Col3|
|---|---|---|
|||**5**|

||**Service Performance Dashboard Overview**|



### p46_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Dashboard Tab|Information Provided|
|---|---|
|TE Tunnel|For the selected Traffic Engineering (TE) tunnel circuit, the dashboard<br>displays details, such as<br>• name<br>• type<br>• creation date<br>• service statistics<br>• outgoing traffic,<br>• bandwidth utilization<br>• reserved bandwidth, and<br>• service availability|
|SR Policy|For the selected Segment Routing (SR) policy, the dashboard displays<br>details, such as<br>• name<br>• serviceability state<br>• associated endpoint<br>• service statistics<br>• outgoing traffic<br>• bandwidth utilization<br>• reserved bandwidth, and<br>• service availability|

## Page 47

### p47_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Get Started with Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager (Cisco EPN Manager)|Col2|
|---|---|
|**Service Performance Dashboard Overview**||



### p47_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Dashboard Tab|Information Provided|
|---|---|
|CE/L3VPN|For the selected circuit or VC, the dashboard displays details, such as<br>• name<br>• discovery state, and<br>• last modified date<br>• inbound and outbound QoS drops<br>• service traffic<br>• two-way delay<br>• one-way jitter<br>• service loss, and<br>• end-to-end performance statistics for service probes with a<br>cross-launch to the IPSLA dashboard for EVCs or to the Y.1731<br>dashboard for L3VPN services.<br>**Note**<br>You can toggle between inbound and outbound data. In the** Top N**<br>**Service QoS Class Traffic** dashlet, you can also toggle between pre<br>and postpolicy data.|
|Top CE/L3VPN|Lists the circuits and VCs with the highest values for parameters, such as<br>• delay<br>• jitter<br>• service loss, and<br>• traffic (both inbound and outbound)<br>You can toggle between CE and L3VPN services information.<br>**Note**<br>For large L3VPN circuits with more than 2000 endpoints, this data cannot<br>be displayed.|

## Page 48

### p48_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Get Started with Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager (Cisco EPN Manager)|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Performance Dashboard Overview**|



### p48_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Dashboard > Performance > any of|the tabs that are described in the following table.|
|---|---|
|**Dashboard Tab**|**Information Provided**|
|Device|For the selected device:<br>• Device Memory Utilization Trend—displays the memory<br>utilization graphs for the device. You can choose the required<br>time frame and dates from the drop-down/checkboxes (Zoom<br>and Date).<br>• Device CPU Utilization Trend—displays the CPU utilization<br>graphs for the device. You can choose the required time frame<br>and dates from the drop-down/checkboxes (Zoom and Date).<br>• Device Health information—displays various device health<br>information such as temperature, alarms, events, and reachability.<br>You can choose the required time frame and dates from the<br>drop-down/checkboxes (Zoom and Date).<br>• Device Port Summary—displays the port summary. You can<br>click the** Down Ports** to view details about ports that are down.<br>• Device Availability Trend—displays the device availability<br>graphs (against time) for the device. You can choose the required<br>time frame and dates from the drop-down/checkboxes (Zoom<br>and Date).<br>• Custom MIB Table View and Custom MIB Graph<br>View—displays custom MIB information (if any).|



### p48_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Col1|Col2|Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager 7.0 User and Administrator Guide|

## Page 49

### p49_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Get Started with Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager (Cisco EPN Manager)|Col2|
|---|---|
|**Performance Dashboard Overview**||



### p49_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Dashboard Tab|Information Provided|
|---|---|
|Interfaces|For the selected interface:<br>• Details such as its name, the IP address of the device it is located<br>on, and its configured speed.<br>• The average, minimum, and maximum values for the following<br>performance metrics (you can toggle between the metrics<br>collected for inbound and outbound data):<br>• Traffic<br>• Utilization<br>• Errors<br>• Discards<br>• Cyclic redundancy check (CRC) errors<br>**Note**<br>CRC error data is not polled by default. To enable the<br>collection of this data, choose a polling frequency for the<br>Interface Health monitoring policy's CRC parameter (see<br>Change the Polling for a Monitoring Policy).<br>• Individual graphs that chart the performance metrics listed in the<br>**Interface Statistics** dashlet<br>• Interface availability<br>• Top N QoS class map policy graph (inbound and outbound<br>prepolicy rate, postpolicy rate, and drops percentage)<br>• QoS class map policy statistics (inbound and outbound)|
|QoS|For the selected QoS policy:<br>• Summary information<br>• Statistics and graphs for prepolicy, postpolicy, and dropped class<br>map traffic.<br>• Statistics and graphs for conforming, exceeding, and violating<br>class map traffic|
|IP SLA|For Layer 3 services on the selected probe:<br>• Summary information<br>• IP Service Level Agreement (SLA) statistics<br>• Delay, jitter, and frame loss between endpoints<br>• Endpoint availability|



### p49_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager 7.0 User and Administrator Guide|Col2|Col3|
|---|---|---|
|||**9**|

## Page 50

### p50_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Get Started with Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager (Cisco EPN Manager)|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Performance Dashboard Overview**|



### p50_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Dashboard Tab|Information Provided|
|---|---|
|Y1731|For Layer 2 services on the selected probe:<br>• Summary information<br>• ITU-T Y.1731 statistics<br>• Delay, jitter, frame loss, and CCM frame loss between endpoints<br>• Jitter Bins Statistics<br>• Delay Bins Statistics<br>• Endpoint availability<br>**Note**<br>Bins statistics data is not polled by default. To enable the collection<br>of this data, choose a polling frequency for Bins Statistics parameters<br>in IP SLA Y.1731 Monitoring Policy (see Change the Polling for a<br>Monitoring Policy).|
|Optical SFPs|For the selected Small Form-Factor Pluggable (SFP) Transceiver<br>Module interface:<br>• Details such as its name, the name, and IP address of the device<br>on which the interface is located, and its configured speed.<br>• The average, minimum, and maximum values for the following<br>operating metrics for a device:<br>• Optical input and output power<br>• Operating temperature<br>• Transceiver supply voltage<br>• Laser bias current<br>For the selected Quad Small Form-Factor Pluggable (QSFP)<br>Transceiver Module interface:<br>Individual lane average, minimum, and maximum values for:<br>• Temperature<br>• Voltage<br>• Current<br>• Tx power<br>• Rx power<br>• Individual graphs that chart the operating metrics listed in the<br>**SFP Statistics** dashlet|

## Page 51

### p51_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Get Started with Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager (Cisco EPN Manager)|Col2|
|---|---|
|**Performance Dashboard Overview**||



### p51_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Dashboard Tab|Information Provided|
|---|---|
|SONET/TDM Interfaces|For the selected SONET or time-division multiplexing (TDM)<br>interface:<br>• Details such as its name, configured speed, and the IP address<br>of the device it is located on.<br>• The average, minimum, and maximum values for the following<br>performance metrics:<br>• Interface Details<br>• Interface Statistics<br>• Severely Errored Seconds<br>• Unavailable Seconds<br>• Errored Seconds<br>• P-bit Severely Errored Seconds<br>• CP-bit Severely Errored Seconds<br>• Code Violations<br>• C-bit Errored Seconds<br>• Severely Errored Framing Seconds<br>• C-bit Code Violations<br>• Controlled Slip Seconds<br>• Bursty Errored Seconds<br>• Degraded Minutes<br>Values are provided for both the near-end (the receiving end)<br>and far-end (the transmitting end) of the interface.<br>• Individual graphs that chart the performance metrics listed in the<br>**SONET/TDM Statistics** dashlet|

|---|---|
||**Network Summary Dashboard Overview**|



### p52_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Dashboard Tab|Information Provided|
|---|---|
|Device Sensors|For each sensor of the selected device:<br>• Sensor Name<br>• Sensor Description<br>• Equipment Name<br>• Type<br>• Current value<br>• Unit<br>• Status<br>Click the** i** icon on the current value to view the trend over last 6 hours.|
|MPLS Links Latency|You can get the following details for the link you select:<br>• Link details such as the link name, endpoint device and interface.<br>• Link delay (one-way and two-way).<br>**Note**<br>You can click Link Name in the Top N MPLS Links Table to launch<br>the MPLS links dashboard on the selected link.|

## Page 53

### p53_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Get Started with Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager (Cisco EPN Manager)|Col2|
|---|---|
|**Network Summary Dashboard Overview**||



### p53_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Dashboard Tab|Information Provided|
|---|---|
|Network Devices|• Status (ICMP reachability, SNMP reachability, device manageability), system health,<br>and alarm summary metric dashlets<br>Note the following:<br>• To open a pop-up window that describes the information provided by a metric<br>dashlet, place your cursor over its name and then click the** ?** icon.<br>• To open a page that lists the alarms or devices that correspond to a particular<br>metric, click a dashlet value. For example, if the** SNMP Reachability Status**<br>dashlet indicates that 50 devices are currently reachable via SNMP, click** 50**<br>to open the** Network Devices** page and view a listing of these devices.<br>• Top N devices by CPU utilization, memory utilization, and environmental<br>temperature<br>For the** Top N Environmental Temperature** dashlet, note the following:<br>• Two temperature values are provided for each device: its highest recorded<br>internal temperature (displayed in the** Max Inlet Temp** column) and its highest<br>recorded ambient temperature (displayed in the** Max Other Temp** column).<br>By default, devices are sorted by their internal temperature.<br>• To identify the sensor that recorded a particular temperature value, place your<br>cursor over its_ i_ (**information**) icon.|
|Incidents|• System health and alarm summary metric dashlets<br>Note the following:<br>• To open a pop-up window that describes the information provided by a metric<br>dashlet, place your cursor over its name and then click the** ?** icon.<br>• To open a page that lists the alarms that correspond to a particular metric, click<br>a dashlet value. For example, if the** Alarm Summary** dashlet indicates that 12<br>critical alarms have been raised in your network, click** 12** to open the** Alarms**<br>page and view a listing of these alarms.<br>• Alarm count for the entire network and the Cisco EPN Manager server<br>• Top N alarm types<br>• Syslog summary<br>• Top N event types and their count<br>• Top N devices by number of syslogs sent<br>• Syslog details such as the corresponding device, severity, and message text<br>• Top N devices by number of alarms raised|

## Page 57

### p57_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Get Started with Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager (Cisco EPN Manager)|Col2|
|---|---|
|**How to Use the Dashboards**||



### p57_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|1|Dashboard filters—Filters all dashlets in the dashboard according to the selection. In this example, a<br>time-based filter is used. The filters displayed depend on the dashboard type. For example, in the<br>performance dashboards, you must select a specific interface, device, circuit, or VC.|
|---|---|
|2|Metric dashlets—Provides quick metrics for alarms, available devices, and so forth.|
|3|Dashboard settings and controls:<br>• Dashboard icons—Allows you to launch online help, refresh the entire dashboard, and open the<br>**Dock** window.<br>• Dashboard** Settings** menu—Allows you to add or rename a dashboard tab, add new dashlets (both<br>standard and metric), adjust the dashboard's layout, reset all dashboards to their default settings,<br>and export data from the selected dashlets.<br>**Note**<br>The newly added or a renamed dashboard tab can be viewed only in the Tab view. This change<br>is not reflected in the Dashboard menu.|
|4|Standard dashlets—Provides at-a-glance data that is relevant to the dashboard.|

## Page 63

### p63_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Get Started with Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager (Cisco EPN Manager)|Col2|
|---|---|
|**Manage Jobs Using the Jobs Dashboard**||



### p63_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Button|Description|
|---|---|
|**Delete Job**|Removes a job from the** Jobs** dashboard.|
|**Edit Job**|Edit the settings configured for the selected job.|
|**Edit Schedule**|Displays the series schedule and lets you edit it (start time, interval, and end time).<br>**Note**<br>Editing the schedule of an already-scheduled job will change the status of that job to<br>**Pending for Approval** since each edit requires an approval from the user who created<br>the job.|
|**Run**|Runs a new instance of the selected job. Use this to rerun partially successful or failed<br>jobs; the job will only run for the failed or partially successful components.|
|**Abort**|Stops a currently-running job, but allows you to rerun it later. Not all jobs can be aborted;<br>Cisco EPN Manager will indicate when this is the case.|
|**Cancel Series**|Stops a currently-running job and does not allow anyone to rerun it. If the job is part of<br>a series, future runs are not affected.|
|**Pause Series**|Pauses a scheduled job series. When a series is paused, you cannot run any instances<br>of that series (using** Run**).|
|**Resume Series**|Resumes a scheduled job series that has been paused.|



### p63_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager 7.0 User and Administrator Guide|Col2|Col3|
|---|---|---|
|||**23**|

## Page 91

### p91_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Manage the Inventory|Col2|
|---|---|
|**How Is Inventory Collected?**||



### p91_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Inventory<br>Collection Trigger|Description|
|---|---|
|In response to<br>incoming events|Cisco EPN Manager receives an incoming NE SNMP trap, syslog, or TL1 message that<br>signals a change on the NE. These incoming events include:<br>• Configuration change events that signal a change in the device configuration. These<br>events are normally syslogs or traps.<br>• Other inventory events, such as tunnel up/down, link up/down, module in/out, and<br>so forth.<br>Cisco EPN Manager reacts to these incoming events by collecting NE inventory and<br>state information to make sure that information in its database conforms to that of the<br>NE. Most events trigger granular inventory collection, where Cisco EPN Manager only<br>collects data relevant to the change event; other events will trigger a complete collection<br>(sync) of the NE physical and logical inventory. The data that Cisco EPN Manager<br>collects is determined by information in the incoming event, along with metadata that<br>is defined in Cisco EPN Manager. The metadata in Cisco EPN Manager uses a<br>combination of mechanisms—expedited events, reactive inventory, and granular<br>polling—to fine-tune what is collected.<br>For example, if Cisco EPN Manager receives a GMPLS Tunnel State Change event, it<br>will collect ODU tunnel inventory information to discover midpoints and the Z endpoint<br>of the tunnel.|
|On demand|Users can perform an immediate inventory collection (called_ Sync_) from:<br>• Network Devices page—Select one or more devices (by checking check boxes)<br>and click** Sync**.<br>• Device 360 view—Choose** Actions** >** Sync Now**.<br>See Collect a Device's Inventory Now (Sync), on page 462.|
|Scheduled (daily)|Normal inventory collection is usually performed overnight. Users with sufficient<br>privileges can check when inventory is collected and the status of collection jobs by<br>choosing** Administration** >** Dashboards** >** Job Dashboard** and choosing** System**<br>**Jobs > Inventory and Discovery Jobs.**|



### p91_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager 7.0 User and Administrator Guide|Col2|Col3|
|---|---|---|
|||**51**|

||**Device Reachability and Admin States**|



### p106_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Icon|Device<br>Reachability<br>State|Description|Troubleshooting|
|---|---|---|---|
||Reachable|Cisco Evolved<br>Programmable Network<br>Manager can reach the<br>device using SNMP, or<br>the NCS 2K device<br>using ICMP.|—|
||Ping<br>reachable|Cisco Evolved<br>Programmable Network<br>Manager can reach the<br>device using Ping, but<br>not via SNMP.|Although ICMP ping is successful, check for all possible<br>reasons why SNMP communication is failing. Check<br>that device SNMP credentials are the same in both the<br>device and in Cisco Evolved Programmable Network<br>Manager, whether SNMP is enabled on the device, or<br>whether the transport network is dropping SNMP<br>packets due to reasons such as mis-configuration, etc.<br>See Change Basic Device Properties, on page 324.|
||Unreachable|Cisco Evolved<br>Programmable Network<br>Manager cannot reach<br>the device using Ping.|Verify that the physical device is operational and<br>connected to the network.|
||Unknown|Cisco Evolved<br>Programmable Network<br>Manager cannot connect<br>to the device.|Check the device.|

### p111_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Possible Cause|Recommended Action|
|---|---|
|Connection to the device failed|Verify that the device accepts incoming CLI/ SNMP<br>connections and retry.|
|Connection to the device is closed|Verify that the device accepts incoming CLI/ SNMP<br>connections and retry.|
|Data cap exceeded|Collection Error: Please contact the administrator with<br>inventory logs.|
|Unexpected condition in the TL1 protocol|Verify that the device accepts incoming TL1<br>connections and retry.|
|General unexpected condition in the HTTP protocol|Verify that the device accepts incoming HTTP<br>connections and retry.|

|Error in the CLI_SESSION_SCRIPT document|Verify that the device can accept a new CLI session<br>and retry.|
|A pattern was matched indicating an error during<br>session setup or tear down|Verify that the device can accept a new CLI session<br>and retry.|
|Device not reachable|Please contact the administrator with inventory logs.|
|Failsafe timeout occurred when trying to communicate<br>with the device|Verify device responsiveness and load.|

## Page 114

### p114_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Manage the Inventory|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Import Location Groups**|



### p114_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Device Type|Devices are grouped by family (for example, Optical Networking, Routers,<br>Switches and Hubs, and so forth). Under each device family, devices are<br>further grouped by series. New devices are automatically assigned to the<br>appropriate family and series groups. For example, a Cisco ASR 9006<br>would belong to Routers (family) and Cisco ASR 9000 Series Aggregation<br>Services Routers (series).<br>Note the following:<br>• You cannot create a device type group; these are dynamic groups that<br>are system-defined. Instead, use device criteria to create a user-defined<br>group and give it an appropriate device type name.<br>• Device type groups are not displayed in Network Topology maps.|No|
|---|---|---|
|Location|Location groups allow you to group devices by location. You can create<br>a hierarchy of location groups(such as theater, country, region, campus,<br>building, and floor) by adding devices manually or by adding devices<br>dynamically.<br>A device should appear in one location group only, though a higher level<br>“parent” group will also contain that device.<br>By default, the top location of the hierarchy is the** All Locations** group.<br>All devices that have not been assigned to a location appear under the<br>Unassigned group under All Locations.|Yes|
|User Defined|Devices are grouped by a customizable combination of device and location<br>criteria. You can customize group names and use whatever device and<br>location criteria you need.|Yes|



### p114_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Col1|Col2|Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager 7.0 User and Administrator Guide|

Instead, use device criteria to<br>create a user-defined group, and create subgroups under the<br>user-defined group.|No; instead create a<br>User Defined Group|
|System Defined|Grouped by port usage or state. Ports on new devices are<br>automatically assigned to the appropriate port group.<br>Wireless and Data Center devices use the other System Defined<br>port groups: AVC Configured Interfaces, UCS Interfaces, UCS<br>Uplink Interfaces, WAN Interfaces, and so forth.<br>You cannot create System Defined Port groups. Instead, use device<br>criteria to create a user-defined group, and create subgroups under<br>the user-defined group.<br>**Note**<br>As the WAN Interfaces is a static group, automatic port addition<br>is not applicable. Hence, you must add the ports manually to the<br>group.|No; instead create a<br>User Defined Group|
|User Defined|Grouped by a customizable combination of port criteria, and you<br>can name the group. If the group is dynamic and a port matches the<br>criteria, it is added to the group.|Yes|

### p126_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Col1|Device type, OS type and version, last configuration change, memory<br>utilization, CPU utilization, and last inventory collection. Icons convey the<br>status of the device.<br>Note<br>• If you have opened the Device 360 view for a Cisco NCS 6000 series<br>device that houses a Secure Domain Router (SDR), the SDR's name<br>is also displayed.<br>• If you have opened the Device 360 view for a Cisco Catalyst 6500<br>series device with dual and quad-supervisor Virtual Switching System<br>(VSS), the device's redundancy state, switch mode, and operational<br>redundancy mode are also displayed.<br>Using the menus in the pop-up window, you can also perform these tasks:<br>• Auto-Refresh—For real-time updates of the device status and<br>troubleshooting, enable an on-demand refresh by clicking the Refresh<br>icon. Alternatively, you can set the autorefresh interval to 30 seconds,<br>1 minute, 2 minutes, or 5 minutes from the drop-down list. Auto-Refresh<br>is OFF by default.<br>Note<br>The Auto-Refresh setting is applicable only for the open 360 view<br>pop-up window. If the view is closed and reopened, or another view<br>is opened, by default Auto-Refresh turns Off.<br>• Troubleshoot—Perform a ping or traceroute, or launch the alarm<br>browser (Actions menu).<br>• Performance—Check device CPU and memory (View > Performance<br>Graphs).<br>• Topology—View the network topology and device's local topology,<br>up to three hops (Actions > > Network Topology menu).<br>• Open the Device Console to enter commands you want to run<br>(Actions > Device Console).<br>• Collect the device's inventory and save it to the database using Actions ><br>Sync Now.<br>• Open an HTTP, HTTPS, SSH, or Telnet session with the device<br>(Actions > Connect To Device).<br>• Launch Cisco Transport Controller for optical devices (Actions menu).<br>• Enables you to resync the condition of the selected Cisco NCS 2000<br>series device with severity NA/NR using Resync Conditions (Actions<br>menu).<br>• Open the Device Details page to view the details about software image<br>and configuration file management, and use the device's Chassis View<br>(by clicking the device IP address hyperlink or choosing View > Chassis<br>View).|

### p127_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Col1|• Open the Configuration page to perform any configuration changes on<br>the device, without navigating from the Device 360 page. Choose<br>View > Configuration.<br>Note<br>This option is available on devices where configuration changes can<br>be performed. For example, Cisco NCS 2000 series devices.<br>• Select a device for a side-by-side comparison with another device based<br>on information such as raised alarms and status of circuits, interfaces,<br>and modules (Actions > Add to Compare)—see Compare Device<br>Information and Status.<br>• Click Device OAM in the Actions menu to do a ping test or traceroute<br>between two devices. |Performance Graphs|Charts reflecting various aspects of the device performance. |Modules|Modules that are configured on the device, including their name, type, state,<br>ports, and location.|
|Interfaces|Interfaces that are configured on the device, including status information.<br>You can also launch an Interface 360 view for a specific interface.|
|Neighbors|NEs that are connected to this device through Cisco Discovery Protocol<br>(CDP). If the selected device does not support CDP, this tab is empty.<br>Displayed information includes device type and name, and local and device<br>ports. To view the neighbors in a pop up topology map, choose** Actions >**<br>**N Hop Topology** (see View a Device's Local Topology from the Device 360<br>View, on page 89).<br>**Note**<br>This option is not available for Cisco NCS 1010 devices.|
|Circuit/VCs|Circuit/VC name, type, customer, status, and creation date for each circuit<br>provisioned on the device. You can also launch a Circuit/VC 360 view for<br>specific circuits/VCs.<br>**Note**<br>This option is not available for Cisco NCS 1010 devices.|
|Satellites tab|For Cisco ASR 9000 series devices in a cluster configuration, this tab lists<br>the satellite’s name, type, description, status, IP address, and MAC address.<br>You can also launch a Satellite 360 view for a specific satellite.|

### p132_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Tab Name|Description|
|---|---|
|Chassis<br>View|Provides inventory, service, and alarm information that is contextualized to the element you<br>select. (To configure<br>elements that are grouped according to their logical function, click the** Device Details** tab.)<br>See Ways to Configure Devices Using Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager, on<br>page 321.|

For links to topics that describe other<br>ways to view interface information in Cisco EPN Manager, see View Device Interfaces, on<br>page 102.|
|Circuits|View the circuits a device, card, or port participates in. For links to topics that describe other<br>ways to view circuit information in Cisco EPN Manager, see View Circuits/VCs, on page 110.|
|Image|Manage the software image that is running on the device. See View the Images That Are<br>Saved in the Image Repository, on page 134.<br>**Note**<br>This tab is only available when a top-level chassis is selected.|
|Configuration<br>Archive|Manage the device configuration file that is running on the device. See View All Archived<br>Files.<br>**Note**<br>This tab is only available when a top-level chassis is selected.|

|**How Do I Determine When Files Are Last Archived?**||



### p157_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Use this field:|To purge files when:|
|---|---|
|Maximum configuration archive versions<br>to be retained per device|The number of a device’s configuration files exceed this setting (5 by default).|
|Maximum days to retain configuration<br>archive|A configuration file’s age exceeds this setting (7 days by default). However,<br>it should be noted that configurations are purged only when a new version is<br>created, ensuring that at least one version is always retained for recovery.<br>**Note**<br>Configuration archive feature retains at least one version of the configuration<br>regardless of the specified retention period. This ensures that a baseline<br>configuration is available for recovery purposes, especially in emergency<br>situations. Purging of configuration files occurs only when a new<br>configuration version is created.|

## Page 234

### p234_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Visualize the Network|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Link Serviceability States**|



### p234_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Span Loss|Channel span loss data is displayed along with the minimum and maximum threshold<br>and resolution. If the span loss data is out of range, it is displayed in red.|
|---|---|
|Alarms|Current alarms for the link, including their severity, status, the time they were<br>generated, the source of the alarm, and the alarm's ID. Also provides a launch point<br>for the Alarm Browser.|
|Links|(LAGs only) Status, name, and IP address for the A-side and Z-side port in the Link<br>Aggregation Group.|
|Endpoints|Devices and interfaces that serve as endpoints for the link. Provides a launch point<br>for the Interface 360 view. For optical devices, this tab also displays the latest<br>recorded power values for transmitted and received signals.<br>**Note**<br>Power values are not normally displayed for manual links. However, if you open<br>the Link 360 view for a manual LMP or OTS link between a Cisco NCS 1000 and<br>2000 device, the view displays the power values for both endpoints.|
|Circuit/VCs|(For a circuit/VC that traverses the link) Circuit/VC name, type, customer, status,<br>and creation date. Also provides a launch point for the Circuit/VC 360 view.|
|SRRGs|Lists the Shared Risk Resource Groups (SRRGs) assigned to the link or to the link<br>endpoint devices. For each listed SRRG, you can see whether it is the default SRRG<br>on the link/device or if it has been assigned to the link/device. For more information<br>about SRRGs, see View and Manage Shared Risk Resource Groups (SRRG) in the<br>Geo Map.|
|APC|Lists the sides, admin status, APC status, and progress status of the link.|



### p234_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Serviceability<br>State|Icon|Description|
|---|---|---|
|Admin Down||Link was purposefully shut down by the administrator.|
|Down||Link is down (but it should not be).|
|Up||Link is up and traffic is passing through the link.|
|Auto Up||Link is up because it detected a signal (this state is only supported by optical<br>devices).|
|Unavailable||Link is not discovered yet or its status is unavailable.|



### p234_default_t4 (default, high confidence)

## Page 238

### p238_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Visualize the Network|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Troubleshoot Link Issues**|



### p238_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Link Issue|Possible Cause|Solution|
|---|---|---|
|Links that previously existed<br>disappear from the topology map.|The hostname might have been<br>changed on one of the endpoint<br>devices.|**1.**<br>Delete the device on which the<br>hostname was changed from<br>the system and then add it<br>again.<br>**2.**<br>Sync the device and all devices<br>connected to it to make sure<br>that all information is updated.|



### p238_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Col1|Col2|Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager 7.0 User and Administrator Guide|
|---|---|---|
|**198**|||

## Page 242

### p242_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Visualize the Network|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Add a Background Image to the Network Topology**|



### p242_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Procedure|Col2|Col3|
|---|---|---|
||**Command or Action**|**Purpose**|
|**Step 1**|Symmetrical (default)—Maintains the symmetry that is<br>inherent in the topology. This ensures that adjacent nodes<br>are closer to each other and prevents node overlapping.||
|**Step 2**|Circular—Arranges the network elements in a circular style<br>highlighting the clusters inherent in the network topology.||
|**Step 3**|Hierarchical—Ensures that the dependencies on the<br>relationships and flows between elements are maintained.||
|**Step 4**|Incremental—Maintains the relative positions of specific<br>elements while adjusting the positions of newly added<br>elements. Use this layout to re-render nodes/links and to<br>clean up overlaps.||



### p242_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Col1|Col2|Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager 7.0 User and Administrator Guide|
|---|---|---|
|**202**|||

|Monitor the Network|Col2|
|---|---|
||**View OTDR Scan Results in the Geo Map**|



### p290_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Procedure|Col2|Col3|
|---|---|---|
||**Command or Action**|**Purpose**|
|**Step 1**|Launch the OTDR scan.||
|**Step 2**|Define the scan parameters and run the scan.||
|**Step 3**|Click** View on Geo Map**.|The geo map opens. The OTDR scan results graph is<br>displayed on the left. The geo map zooms to show the<br>relevant devices, link and fiber (highlighted in purple).|
|**Step 4**|Click on a point in the OTDR scan results graph.|A location icon appears on the exact location on the fiber<br>on the geo map and a popup panel provides information<br>about that location, including the distance in kilometers<br>along the fiber, the exact coordinates, and the physical<br>address.<br>**Note**<br>If the exact location cannot be calculated, the location icon<br>shows an approximate location that is within a certain<br>radius of the exact location. The radius (in km) is shown<br>in the popup panel and a circle around the location icon in<br>the map indicates that this is an approximate location within<br>a radius of the exact location.|



### p290_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Col1|Col2|Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager 7.0 User and Administrator Guide|

Proceed with alarm acknowledgment?**|
|**Disable**<br>**confirmation**<br>**prompt for**<br>**“Clear all of this**<br>**condition”**|Disables the following message from displaying when user selects an alarm and chooses<br>**Change Status** >** Clear all of this condition**:<br>**Are you sure you want to clear all alarms of this condition?**<br>(Disabled by default)|

### p302_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|To find these alarms:|Choose Monitor > Monitoring Tools > Alarms and Events and:|
|---|---|
|Alarms generated by a<br>specific device|For active alarms, click the**_ i_** icon next to the device name to open the Device 360<br>view, then click the** Alarms** tab. For cleared alarms, refer to the Alarms and Events<br>table.<br>**Note**<br>• For Cisco NCS 2000 series devices, transient conditions are processed as<br>alarms and displayed in the Alarms table. Click**_ i_** to navigate to the related<br>port through the Interface 360 view. This feature is enabled only when you<br>select the** Enable Transient Condition Alarms** check box in** Alarm Other**<br>**Settings** page.<br>Enabling the** Transient Condition Alarms** feature requires selecting the<br>corresponding check box on the** Alarm Other Settings** page. If you disable<br>this feature after an alarm has been triggered, the alarm will continue to be<br>displayed on the** Alarms** tab.<br>• For SVO devices, clicking the device name hyperlink cross launches the<br>SVO UI. The SVO device hyperlink is enabled only if you have selected<br>the** Enable Alarms Cross Launch to SVO** check box in the** Alarm Other**<br>**Settings** page.<br>For cleared alarms or correlated alarms, click the appropriate tab and enter the<br>device name or component in the** Location** column. You can use wild cards.<br>For certain devices, you can also use the Chassis View to check device alarms.<br>See View Alarms in the Chassis View, on page 99.|
|Alarms generated by a<br>specific circuit/VC|**1.**<br>Click the**_ i_** icon next to the device name to open the Device 360 view, then<br>click the** Circuit/VC** tab.<br>**2.**<br>Click the**_ i_** icon next to the Circuit/VC name to open the Circuit/VC 360 view,<br>then click the** Alarms** tab.<br>See Check Circuits/VCs for Faults, on page 679 for more circuit/VC alarm<br>information.|

## Page 303

### p303_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Monitor the Network|Col2|
|---|---|
|**Find and View Alarms**||



### p303_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|To find these alarms:|Choose Monitor > Monitoring Tools > Alarms and Events and:|
|---|---|
|All alarms in the network|Click the** Show Alarm History** link.|
|Alarms assigned to you|Click the** Show** drop-down filter list and choose** Assigned to me**. You can also<br>use this filter in the Cleared/Correlated alarms tabs.|
|Unassigned alarms|Click the** Show** drop-down filter list and choose** Unassigned Alarms**. You can<br>also use this filter in the Cleared/Correlated alarms tabs.|
|Cleared Alarms|Click the** Show** drop-down filter list and choose** Cleared Alarms** Alarms. You<br>can also use this filter in the Cleared/Correlated alarms tabs.|
|Network Alarms|Under the** Alarms** tab, click** Network Alarms** tab to view all network impacting<br>alarms.<br>This tab is enabled only if you have selected the** Enable Network Alarms View**<br>check box in** Alarm Other Settings** page.|
|Latest alarms according<br>to the Cisco EPN<br>Manager timestamp|For active alarms:<br>• Alarms in the last 30 minutes—Click the Show drop-down filter and choose<br>the last 5, 15, or 30 minutes** (CEPNM timestamp)**.<br>• Alarms in the last 24 hours—Click the Show drop-down filter and choose<br>the last 1, 8, or 24 hours** (CEPNM timestamp)**.<br>• Alarms in the last 7 days—Click the Show drop-down filter and choose the<br>last 7 days** (CEPNM timestamp)**.<br>You can use these same filters for cleared and correlated alarms. The filters do<br>not have the** (CEPNM timestamp)** suffix because filtering by device timestamps<br>is not supported for cleared and correlated alarms. For more information on<br>**(CEPNM timestamp)** and** (Device timestamp)**, see Device Timestamp and<br>CEPNM Timestamp, on page 265.|
|Latest alarms according<br>to the device timestamp|Follow the same instructions given in the previous row, but choose the filters with<br>the suffix** (Device timestamp)** This filter is not supported when searching for<br>cleared or correlated alarms.|
|All alarms generated by<br>a device group, series, or<br>type|Choose a group from the navigation pane on the left. You can also use this filter<br>for cleared and correlated alarms.|

### p357_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Date/Time|Date and time when the section monitoring data was<br>collected for the device. The value in this column<br>depends on the report interval that you chose when<br>you created the report. The report interval can be 15<br>minutes or 24 hours.|
|BBE-SM|Number of background block errors for the device.|
|BBER-SM|Background block error ratio for the device.|
|ES-SM|Number of errored seconds for the device.|
|ESR-SM|Errored seconds ratio for the device.|
|SES-SM|Number of severely errored seconds for the device.|
|SESR-SM|Severely errored seconds ratio for the device.|
|UAS-SM|Number of unavailable seconds for the device.|
|FC-SM|Number of failure counts (AIS/RFI detected) for the<br>device.|

|Enabled the periodic collection.|For any System Monitoring Periodic reports<br>(CPU/Disk/Memory), the periodic collection must be<br>enabled. Once enabled, the report must be generated<br>after 12 hours to see the output.<br>**Note**<br>To enable Periodic collection,<br>• Visit link:**` https://`****_`<Server`_**<br>**_`IP>`_****`/webacs/ncsDiag.jsp`**<br>• Select** System Monitoring Diagnostic** ><br>**Monitoring Settings**, and click the** Periodic**<br>**Collection Enable** button.|
|Chosen the correct device type for a particular report.|Do not choose NCS devices for generating CE<br>Performance reports as they are optical devices.|
|Selected the correct time period while generating a<br>report.|You cannot choose a 2-week time period if you<br>enabled the policy only two days ago.|

|Successful device inventory collection. For more<br>details, see Find Devices With Inventory Collection<br>or Discovery Problems, on page 70|For the reports to have data, the inventory collection<br>status must be** Completed**.|

A primary interface and its backup interface<br>together make up a Protection Group (denoted by a unique<br>integer). Associating cards with backup members ensures<br>that when the primary interface fails, the protecting<br>interface quickly assumes the traffic load from the primary<br>interface. Cards displayed as the Active members are<br>cards functioning as the protecting members of the<br>service.<br>Ensure that the Primary and Backup members are of the<br>same type. For example, if you choose a T1 interface as<br>a Primary member, the Backup member must also be a<br>T1 interface.<br>Hold-Off Timer is available for 1+1 card protection (NCS<br>42XX devices having IOS-XE version 16.10.1 or higher).<br>It is used to prevent the successive switching in case of<br>network inconsistency. The valid range is 0–10 seconds.<br>Default value is 5.<br>The Admin Mode for the protection group is configured<br>in the order Lockout > Force Switch > Manual Switch ><br>None. For more information about these modes and the<br>revert timer, see the descriptions in Configure APS or<br>MSP and UPSR or SNCP Protection Groups, on page 336.|-|

### p383_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Fields|Descriptions|Values|Descriptions|Applicable<br>Controller<br>Modes|
|---|---|---|---|---|
|Framing|Framing mode<br>used for the<br>CEM channel.|CRC and NO_CRC.|CRC: represents the faming type with cyclic<br>redundancy check.|SONET/<br>SDH|
|Framing|Framing mode<br>used for the<br>CEM channel.|Unframed, DSX1_ESF,<br>DSX1_SF, Auto Detect,<br>C_BIT, and M13.|• Unframed: indicates that a single CEM<br>channel is used for all timeslots.<br>• DSX1_SF: indicates that the DS1 type<br>of interface has the framing type as<br>super frame. SF uses 12 frames per<br>super frame for in-band signaling<br>extraction.<br>• DSX1_ESF: indicates that DS1 type of<br>interface has the framing type as<br>extended super frame. ESF uses 24<br>frames per ESF.|PDH, HOP,<br>LOP, and<br>STS1E.|
|Loopback|Specifies the<br>loopback value<br>associated with<br>the CEM<br>interface.|None, Local, Network Line,<br>Network Payload, Remote<br>Line, and Remote Payload.|For a detailed explanation about the different<br>loopback values, refer the latest IOS<br>Command References.|All|
|Loopback|Specifies the<br>loopback value<br>associated with<br>the CEM<br>interface.|Diag, LocalPayload, Remote<br>- PDH ESF Payload, Remote<br>ESF Line, Remote ESF Line<br>CSU, Remote ESF Line NIU,<br>Remote_IBOC,<br>Remote_IBOC_CSU,<br>Remote_IBOC_FAC1,<br>Remote_IBOC_FAC2,<br>DIAG, and<br>LOCAL_PAYLOAD.|—|PDH|
|Protection<br>Role|Identifies the<br>priority based<br>on which the<br>recovered<br>clock must be<br>obtained.|WORKING|The recovered clock is obtained from a clock<br>with the highest priority.|SONET/<br>SDH|
|Protection<br>Role|Identifies the<br>priority based<br>on which the<br>recovered<br>clock must be<br>obtained.|PROTECT|The recovered clock is obtained from a clock<br>with a lower priority than the primary clock.|SONET/<br>SDH|
|Cable<br>Length|Sets the transmission attenuation according to the length of the cable. For example, if you<br>choose short 110, the cable length is from 0 to 110 feet. Choose Short 220 if the cable length<br>is from 110 to 220 feet, and so on. Your values are between Short 110 to Short 550.|Sets the transmission attenuation according to the length of the cable. For example, if you<br>choose short 110, the cable length is from 0 to 110 feet. Choose Short 220 if the cable length<br>is from 110 to 220 feet, and so on. Your values are between Short 110 to Short 550.|Sets the transmission attenuation according to the length of the cable. For example, if you<br>choose short 110, the cable length is from 0 to 110 feet. Choose Short 220 if the cable length<br>is from 110 to 220 feet, and so on. Your values are between Short 110 to Short 550.|PDH|
|Line Coding|Line encoding method for the controller:<br>• For E1, the options is Alternate Mark Inversion (AMI).<br>• For T1, the options are AMI and bipolar with 8 zero substitution (B8ZS).|Line encoding method for the controller:<br>• For E1, the options is Alternate Mark Inversion (AMI).<br>• For T1, the options are AMI and bipolar with 8 zero substitution (B8ZS).|Line encoding method for the controller:<br>• For E1, the options is Alternate Mark Inversion (AMI).<br>• For T1, the options are AMI and bipolar with 8 zero substitution (B8ZS).|PDH|

### p393_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Fields|Descriptions|
|---|---|
|**Clock > Sync-E Common Properties (Global Level)**|**Clock > Sync-E Common Properties (Global Level)**|
|Automatic Selection process|Indicates the type of method used for synchronization of the clocks. The values<br>are: Automatic, Forced, Manual, and Cisco.<br>Note- You can configure only one interface per synchronization type.|
|Clock Type|Indicates the Ethernet Equipment Clock (EEC) option to be used:<br>Option 1-represents EEC-Option I of the European time zone.<br>Option 2-represents EEC-Option II of the American time zone.|
|QL Mode Enabled|Indicates whether the clock is to be used with the Quality Level (QL) function:<br>Enabled or Disabled.|
|ESMC Enabled|Indicates the status of the Ethernet Synchronization Message Channel (ESMC):<br>Enabled or Disabled.|
|SSM Option|Indicates the Synchronization Status Message (SSM) option being used:<br>Option 1-represents ITU-T Option I<br>Option 2- GEN1-represents ITU-T Option II Generation 1<br>Option 2- GEN2-represents ITU-T Option II Generation 2|
|Hold Off Time (global level)|Indicates the length of time (in milliseconds) for a device to wait before issuing<br>a protection response to a failure event.<br>A valid range is 300–1800 milliseconds.|
|Wait To Restore Time (global level)|Indicates the length of time (in seconds) to wait after a failure is fixed before<br>the span returns to its original state.<br>A valid range is 0–86400 seconds.|
|Revert Enabled|Specifies whether the network clock is to use Revertive mode: Enabled or<br>Disabled.|
|**Sync-E > Interface Input Source (Interface Level) Properties**|**Sync-E > Interface Input Source (Interface Level) Properties**|

### p394_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Configure Devices|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Synchronize the Clock Using Sync-E, BITS, and PTP**|



### p394_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Fields|Descriptions|
|---|---|
|Interface Name|Name and hyperlink of the Gigabit or 10 Gigabit interface associated with<br>Sync-E.|
|Active clock|Indicates whether the interface is currently chosen as the active clock. This<br>interface can either be a primary or secondary interface, however, the interface<br>that is currently enabled for Sync-E is considered to be the active interface.|
|Priority|Indicates the value used for selecting a Sync-E interface for clocking if more<br>than one interface is configured. Values are 1–250, with 1 being the highest<br>priority.<br>The highest priority clock represents the primary clock.|
|Hold Off Time (interface level)|Indicates the length of time (in milliseconds) to wait after a clock source goes<br>down before removing the source.<br>A valid range is a value 300–1800 milliseconds.|
|Wait To Restore Time (interface level)|Indicates the length of time (in seconds) to wait after a failure is fixed before<br>the interface returns to its original state.<br>A valid range is a value 0–86400 seconds.|
|Rx Exact/QL Use|Indicates the QL Receive function with which the clock must be used.|
|Tx Exact/QL Send|Indicates the QL Transmit function with which the clock must be used.|
|**Clock > BITS-Frequency and BITS-Interface Properties**|**Clock > BITS-Frequency and BITS-Interface Properties**|
|Source Slot|Indicates whether the clock source is R0 or R1 (for XE devices).|
|Clock Interface|Indicates whether the clock source is BITS0_IN, BITS0_OUT, BITS1_IN, or<br>BITS1_OUT (for XR devices).|
|Priority|Indicates the value used for selecting a BITS interface for clocking if more<br>than one interface is configured. Values are 1–250, with 1 being the highest<br>priority.<br>The highest priority clock represents the primary clock.|
|Clock Type|Indicates whether the clock type that must be used is from an E1 line or a T1<br>line (for XE devices). For XR devices, the line can be E1, T1, J1, 2M, or 64K.<br>For BITS Interface parameters, the clock type indicates the frequency values<br>that must be associated with the clock.<br>Supported clock types for XE devices:<br>• BITS Frequency: Supported options are 2.048_MHz and 10_MHz.<br>• BITS Interface: Supported options are T1 and E1.<br>Supported clock types for XR devices:<br>• BITS Interface: Supported options are T1, E1, J1, 2M, and 64K.|

|Bits Sub Framing|The supported Bits sub framing values for XR devices with E1 clock type are<br>SA4, SA5, SA6, SA7, and SA8.|
|Line Code|The line code value that must be associated with the BITS interface.<br>Supported line code values for XE devices:<br>• For E1 interface: The values are AMI and HDB3.<br>• For T1 interface: The values are AMI and B8ZS.<br>Supported line code values for XR devices:<br>• For E1 interface: The values are AMI and HDB3.<br>• For J1 interface: The values are AMI and B8ZS.<br>• For T1 interface: The values are AMI and B8ZS.|
|Line Build Out|The line build-out value that must be associated with the BITS interface. This<br>field is supported only for T1 interface.<br>Supported line build-out values for XE devices:<br>• For T1 interface: The values are 0-133ft, 133-266ft, 266-399ft, 399-533ft,<br>and 533-655ft.<br>Supported line build-out values for XR devices:<br>• For T1 BITS0_OUT interface: The values are 0, 1, 2, 3, and 4.<br>• For T1 BITS1_OUT interface: The values are 0, 1, 2, 3, and 4.|

## Page 420

### p420_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Configure Devices|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Configure TCM and TTI Parameters**|



### p420_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Editable TCM Parameters|Descriptions|
|---|---|
|State|Configures the state of TCM properties on the device as enabled or disabled.|
|Signal Failure Threshold|Configures the threshold value for signal failures on ODUk controllers. The<br>values are E6, E7, E8, and E9.|
|Sent SAPI|Configures the source access point identifier of the TTI.<br>Enter a value of up to 14 bytes in length.|
|Sent DAPI|Configures the destination access point identifier of the TTI. Enter a value of<br>up to 14 bytes in length.|
|Sent Operator Specific String Type|Configures the type of the operator-specific string of the TTI as hexadecimal<br>or ASCII type.|
|Sent Operator Specific String|Configures the operator-specific string of the TTI.<br>Enter a value of up to 32 characters in length.|
|Performance Monitor|Enables or disables performance monitoring on an ODUk controller.|
|Signal Degrade Threshold|Configures the signal degrade threshold value.<br>The values are: E6, E7, E8, and E9.|
|Expected SAPI|Configures the current source access point identifier of the TTI. Enter a value<br>of up to 14 bytes in length.|
|Expected DAPI|Configures the current destination access point identifier of the TTI. Enter a<br>value of up to 14 bytes in length.|
|Expected Operator Specific String<br>Type|Configures the type of the operator-specific string of the TTI as hexadecimal<br>or ASCII type.|

|Category|Parameters|Description|

|Common<br>Optics,<br>OTS-OCH,<br>DSP, and<br>DWDM<br>Controller<br>Parameters|• Name<br>• Admin Status<br>• Operational<br>Status<br>• Transport Admin<br>Status|Name- (Display only) Displays the port number.<br>Admin Status-Defines whether the interface is managed (Up), down, or in<br>maintenance mode. You cannot modify the controller properties when the<br>status of the interface is Up.<br>Operational Status – Defines whether the interface is operational and is<br>performing as provisioned.<br>Transport Admin Status – Defines the transport administration state of the<br>controller.|
|Common<br>Optics and<br>DWDM<br>Parameters|• Actual<br>Wavelength (nm)<br>or Actual<br>Frequency (thz)<br>• Wavelength (nm)<br>or Frequency<br>(thz)|Displays the wavelength and frequency utilized by the channel.|

|-|FEC Mode|FEC value to be set on the controllers.<br>Before changing the FEC mode setting, ensure that the admin state of the<br>interface you are trying to modify is in Down (out of service) state with G709<br>configuration enabled.|
|Optics<br>Parameters|Speed|Set the speed values (in gigabits per second) that the controllers must operate<br>on.|
|-|DAC Rate|Select the DAC rate from the drop-down list.|
|-|Min Chromatic<br>Dispersion|Enter the minimum chromatic dispersion value.|
|-|Max Chromatic<br>Dispersion|Enter the maximum chromatic dispersion value.|
|-|Configured Tx Power|Enter the transmit power.|
|-|Modulation Type|Set the modulation type from the drop-down list.|
|-|Differential<br>Modulation|Enable or disable Differential Encoding (DE) based on the configured speed<br>values.|
|-|Loopback|Configure the loopback as:<br>• Internal - All packets are looped back internally within the router before<br>reaching an external interface. It tests the internal Rx to Tx path and<br>stops the traffic to egress out from the Physical port.|

## Page 438

### p438_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Configure Devices|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Configure Controllers (Optics, OTS, OCH, DSP, and DWDM)**|



### p438_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Category|Parameters|Description|
|---|---|---|
|||• Line - Incoming network packets are looped back through the external<br>interface.|
|-|SD BER|Set the signal degrade bit error rate. Your options are E-5, E-6, E-7, E-8, or<br>E-9.|
|-|SF BER|Set the signal fail bit error rate. Your options are E-3, E-4, or E-5.|
|DWDM<br>Parameters|Loopback|Configure the loopback as:<br>• Internal - All packets are looped back internally within the router before<br>reaching an external interface. It tests the internal Rx to Tx path and<br>stops the traffic to egress out from the Physical port.<br>• Line - Incoming network packets are looped back through the external<br>interface.|
|-|• OTU-SD<br>• OTU-SF<br>• ODU-SD<br>• ODU-SF|Configure SF (signal fail) and SD (signal degrade) BER reporting and<br>thresholds.<br>Depending on whether the alarm is an OTU or ODU alarm, the alarm<br>represents that SM BER is in excess based on the SD BER threshold or SF<br>BER threshold.|
|OTS<br>Parameters|Port Role|Current operational state of the port.<br>For a protection switch, the Com work role is displayed, whereas, for an<br>amplifier module, the Com Line/Osc or Com Check role is displayed.|
|-|Rx/Tx Low Threshold<br>(dBm)|Configures the receiver/transponder low receive power threshold. The valid<br>range is from -500 to 300.|
|-|Ampli Channel Power<br>(dBm)|Configures the amplifier per channel power set point. The valid range is -500<br>to 300. The default value is 0.0.|
|-|Channel Power Max<br>Delta (dBm)|Configures the maximum difference among all the measured channel powers.<br>The valid range is 0–200.|
|-|Ampli Gain and Ampli<br>Gain Range|Configures the amplifier gain set point. The valid mode for the range is normal<br>or extended.<br>**Note**<br>The amplifier gain range is configurable only when the controller is in<br>shutdown state.|
|-|Ampli Safety<br>Controller Mode|Configures the safety control mode as auto or disabled.|
|-|OSRI|Configures the optical safety remote interlock as on or off.|
|-|Ampli Tilt|Configures the amplifier tilt using a number between -50 to +50.|

|Create and edit<br>GMPLS UNIs|GMPLS/WSONsub-tab<br>> GMPLS UNIs|• Specify the ingress and egress ports for the GMPLS UNI and choose if<br>the UNI is of numbered or unnumbered type. Ensure that you specify if<br>the UNI is of type UNI-C or UNI-N.<br>• The trunk values are automatically configured to the respective alien<br>wavelength values depending on your GMPLS UNI configuration. If the<br>configured alien wavelength is supported on both trunk ports, then setting<br>it on one of the trunk ports automatically configures the same alien<br>wavelength on both trunk ports.<br>• For Cisco NCS 2000 devices, the GMPLS UNI trunk value can be set<br>to Default.<br>• Specify the local and remote interface IP, and remote system IP and<br>controller. These values enable the remote system connection for the<br>UNI.|

### p452_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Line Card Type|Line Card Configuration<br>Parameters|Descriptions|
|---|---|---|
|SONET|Port Number|The port number of the SONET interface you are configuring.|
|SONET|Port Name|Allows you to add a name for the SONET optical port.|
|SONET|SD BER|Sets the signal degrade bit error rate.|
|SONET|SF BER|Sets the signal fail bit error rate.|
|SONET|Type|Defines the port as SONET or SDH.|
|SONET|Provides Sync|When checked, the card is provisioned as an NE timing reference.|
|SONET|Sync Messaging|Enables synchronization status messages (S1 byte), which allow the node<br>to choose the best timing source.|
|SONET|Admin SSM In|If the node does not receive an SSM signal, it defaults to synchronization<br>traceability unknown (STU). Admin SSM allows you to override the STU<br>value with one of the following:<br>• PRS—Primary reference source (Stratum 1)<br>• STS2—Stratum 2<br>• TNC—Transit node clock<br>• STS3E—Stratum 3E<br>• STS3—Stratum 3<br>• SMC—SONET minimum clock<br>• ST4—Stratum 4|

### p460_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Configure Devices|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Discover and Configure MPLS LDP and MPLS-TE Links**|



### p460_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|MPLS LDP Fields|Field Descriptions|
|---|---|
|LDP Address|Specify the IP address of the LDP interface. Once the LDP address is set, it<br>cannot be edited. To change the LDP address, delete the LDP session and create<br>a new session with the new LDP address.|
|Session Hold Time|(Optional) Enter the time, in seconds, that the LDP session will go down if no<br>hellos have been received after the Hold timer expires. Range is 15 to 65535.|
|NSR Enabled|Choose true or false to either enable or disable LDP nonstop routing (NSR).<br>Enabling NSR allows the LDP to continue to operate across a node failure<br>without losing peer sessions.|
|Discovery Hold time and<br>Discovery Target Hold time|(Optional) Enter the time, in seconds, an LDP source and a discovered LDP<br>neighbor is remembered without receipt of an LDP hello message from the<br>neighbor. Range is 1 to 65535.|
|Discovery Hold Interval and<br>Discovery Target Hold Interval|(Optional) Enter the time duration, in seconds, during which a LDP source and<br>a discovered LDP neighbor is remembered. Range is 1 to 65535.|
|DownStream Min Label and<br>DownStream Max Label|(Optional) Enter the minimum and maximum number of hops permitted in an<br>LSP established by the Downstream on Demand method of label distribution.<br>Range is 16 to 32767 for ISO XE and 16000 to 1048575 for ISO XR devices.|
|DownStream Max Hop Count|(Optional) Enter the number of hops permitted in an LSP established by the<br>Downstream on Demand method of label distribution. Range is 1 to 255.|
|IGP Hold Down Time|(Optional) Enter the time, in seconds, to specify the time for which the declaration<br>of LDP sync state is delayed after session establishment upon link coming up.<br>Range is 1 to 2147483647 millisecond for ISO XE and 5 to 300 milliseconds<br>for ISO XR devices.|
|Entropy Enabled|Choose true or false to either enable or disable the MPLS LDP Entropy Label<br>support feature which helps improve load balancing across MPLS networks<br>using entropy labels.|
|Explicit Null Enabled|(Optional) Enable this value to advertise explicit-null labels for the directly<br>connected route. Values are Yes (enabled) or No (disabled).|
|Initial Back Off and Max Back Off|(Optional) Enter the initial and maximum back off delay value in seconds. Range<br>is 5 to 2147483.|

## Page 468

### p468_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Configure Devices|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Configure BGP**|



### p468_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Fields|Subfield|Descriptions|
|---|---|---|
|||• Allocate Label Custom Policy Name: Choose a custom policy to be associated with<br>the routing process.<br>**Note**<br>The** Allocate Label** and** Allocate Label Custom Policy Name** fields are only applicable<br>for IOS device types.|
||BGP<br>Additional<br>Paths|Specify the details for the paths that enable the advertisement of multiple paths through<br>the same peering session for the same prefix without the new paths implicitly replacing<br>any previous paths.<br>• Additional Paths: Choose whether the device must send, receive, or send and receive<br>additional paths. This is done at the address family level or the neighbor level. During<br>session establishment, the specified BGP neighbors negotiate the Additional Path<br>capabilities (whether they can send and/or receive) between them.<br>**Note**<br>While configuring Cisco CAT65000 devices, you can configure only Install as the<br>additional path value.<br>• Best Value: This field is enabled only when the Additional Paths value that you choose<br>supports the configuration of the Best Value field.|
||BGP<br>Neighbor AF|Specify the address family details that the specified BGP neighbor belongs to:<br>• Neighbor Address: Choose the Router ID of the neighboring router. These values are<br>populated based on the BGP neighbors created in the Neighbor tab. The value can<br>be an IPv4 or an IPv6 address of the format:<br>• A.B.C.D- for IPv4 addresses, where A, B, C, and D are integers ranging 0–255.<br>• xxxx:xxxx:xxxx:xxxx:xxxx:xxxx:xxxx:xxxx - for IPv6 addresses, where x would<br>be a hexadecimal value and where the address uses eight sets of four hexadecimal<br>addresses (16 bits in each set), separated by a colon (:).<br>• Send Label: Choose the type of label that must be associated with the neighbor.<br>• Route Reflector Client: Enable this field to configure the router as the route reflector<br>and the specified neighbor as its client.<br>• AIGP: Select to enable the accumulated interior gateway protocol (AIGP) path<br>attribute.<br>• Send Community: Choose how the community attributes must be sent to an external<br>Border Gateway Protocol (eBGP) neighbor.<br>• Next Hop Self: Select to set the BGP next-hop attribute of routes being advertised<br>over a peering session to the local source address of the session.<br>• Incoming and Outgoing Route Map Name: Choose to indicate whether a route policy<br>must be applied to inbound or outbound updates from the neighbor.|

|Col1|Col2|Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager 7.0 User and Administrator Guide|

## Page 469

### p469_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Configure Devices|Col2|
|---|---|
|**Configure BGP**||



### p469_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Fields|Subfield|Descriptions|
|---|---|---|
||BGPNetwork<br>Mask|• Network Address and Mask: Specify the network IP address and network mask for<br>the specified IP address.<br>• Back Door Route: Enable to set the administrative distance on an external Border<br>Gateway Protocol (eBGP) route to that of a locally sourced BGP route, causing it to<br>be less preferred than an Interior Gateway Protocol (IGP) route.<br>• Network Route Policy Name: Choose the route policy that will be used to select<br>prefixes for label allocation. This enables BGP to allocate labels for all or a filtered<br>set of global routes (as dictated by the route policy).|
|BGP<br>Neighbor<br>tab fields|-|Specify the following values:<br>• Peer AS Number- Enter the value for the autonomous system number using integers<br>in the range 1–4294967295to.<br>• Neighbor Address- Enter the IP address of the BGP neighbor that you want to<br>configure. The value can be an IPv4 or an IPv6 address of the format.<br>• A.B.C.D- for IPv4 addresses, where A, B, C, and D are integers ranging 0–255.<br>• xxxx:xxxx:xxxx:xxxx:xxxx:xxxx:xxxx:xxxx - for IPv6 addresses, where x would<br>be a hexadecimal value and where the address uses eight sets of four hexadecimal<br>addresses (16 bits in each set), separated by a colon (:).<br>• Local AS Number and Action: Specifies an autonomous-system number prepend to<br>the AS_PATH attribute. The range of values is any valid autonomous system number<br>1–65535.<br>• Update Source: Use this option to establish a peer relationship (TCP connection)<br>using the loopback interface as an alternative instead of using the interface closest to<br>the peer router.<br>• Fall-over: Select a value to enable the BGP fast peering session deactivation for<br>improving the convergence and response time to adjacency changes with the specified<br>BGP neighbor.<br>• Password Encryption and Password: Specify whether password encryption is enabled<br>or not, and if enabled, what the password value is.<br>• (View only) Neighbor State: View the connection status of a neighbor device<br>participating in a BGP routing process. The states are: Idle, Connect, Active, Open<br>sent, Open confirm, and Established.<br>The neighbor device generates events only when its connection status is Established.<br>Check the connection status frequently in case there are updates from the device.<br>**Note**<br>The neighbor state value is not updated during a granular inventory sync. To see the<br>updated values, wait for the sync to end successfully.|

|Hello Interval|Number of seconds between OSPF hello packet advertisements sent by OSPF<br>routers. The Cisco default is 10 seconds.|
|Retransmit Interval|Time that will elapse before a packet is resent. The Cisco default is 5 seconds.|
|Transmit Delay|Service speed. The Cisco default is 1 second.|

By default,<br>measures one-way delay and jitter<br>in both directions, and two-way<br>delay and jitter.|**Probe Domain:** Check the checkbox to enable the<br>probe.<br>**Domain Name:** The name of the maintenance<br>domain for the locally defined CFM MEP.<br>**Domain Interface Type:** The source interface type<br>of the locally defined CFM MEP.<br>**Domain Interface Path ID:** The physical or virtual<br>interface name.<br>**Domain MAC Address or MEP-ID:** Choose<br>whether you want to identify the domain by MAC<br>address or by MEP ID and provide the necessary<br>information in the relevant field below. For MEP<br>ID, enter an ID from 1 to 8191.|Optionally, you<br>can specify the<br>type of<br>statistics to<br>measure,<br>whether or not<br>to use bins for<br>aggregate type,<br>probe<br>frequency and<br>duration<br>values, and<br>more. The<br>values you<br>specify will<br>override the<br>default actions.|

The VLAN ID can<br>be between 1 and 4096.<br>Target MPID or MAC Address: Identify the MEP<br>at the destination, either by MPID (1 to 8191) or by<br>MAC Address.<br>CoS Value: The class of service level (0-7) that will<br>be applied to the CFM message for the specified<br>MEP.<br>Local MPID or MAC Address: Identify the MEP at<br>the source, either by MPID (1 to 8191) or by MAC<br>Address.<br>Burst or Continuous: Specify whether a continuous<br>stream of frames or bursts of frames will be sent<br>during the on-demand operation.<br>Aggregation Period: Specify the length of time in<br>seconds during which the performance<br>measurements are conducted, after which the<br>statistics are generated (1-900).||
|EOAM-Configure-Y-<br>1731-PM-Referenced-On-<br>Demand-IOS|Perform real-time troubleshooting<br>of Ethernet services in referenced<br>mode where a previously<br>configured operation is started and<br>run.|Frame Type: The type of probe, either DMMv1 or<br>SLM.<br>Operation Number: The number of the operation<br>being referenced.||
|Remove-CFM-MEP- IOS|Remove the MEP configuration<br>from the device.|Interface Name, Service Instance Number,EVC<br>Name.||

|Remove-CFM-<br>Service-IOS|Remove the CFM service.|Interface Name, Service Instance Number, EVC<br>Name, Domain Name, Level, Service Name.||

## Page 491

### p491_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Configure Devices|Col2|
|---|---|
|**Create a QoS Classification Profile**||



### p491_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Action|Description|Value|
|---|---|---|
|ACL|The packet must be permitted by the specified<br>access control list (ACL).|The name of the ACL. A string of up to<br>32 alphanumeric characters.|
|MPLS - Imposition|The experimental (EXP) bit value on the imposed<br>label entry of the packet must match the MPLS<br>EXP value that you specify. Use either the MPLS<br>Imposition or the MPLS Topmost for matching<br>criteria. Once you have used one of the MPLS<br>criteria, the other one will no longer be available.|A number from 0 to 7. Up to 8<br>comma-separated values can be entered.|
|MPLS - Topmost|The experimental (EXP) bit value in the topmost<br>label must match the MPLS EXP value that you<br>specify.|A number from 0 to 7. Up to 8<br>comma-separated values can be entered.|
|Cascade|This action is used to cascade one class map into<br>another. It can be used when creating a new class<br>map which has classification policies similar to an<br>existing class map.|Reference the child class map.|
|QoSClassification -<br>COS|The packet’s layer 2 class of service (CoS) bit value<br>must match the specified CoS value.|A number from 0 to 7. Up to 8<br>comma-separated values can be entered.|
|QoSClassification -<br>COS - Inner|The specified value must match packet’s inner CoS<br>value of QinQ packets for Layer 2 class of service<br>(CoS) marking.|A number from 0 to 7. Up to 8<br>comma-separated values can be entered.|
|QoSClassification -<br>DSCP|The packet IP differentiated service code point<br>(DSCP) value must match one or more of the<br>specified values.|Valid values are from 0 to 63. Up to 8<br>comma-separated values can be entered.|
|QoSClassification -<br>DSCP - IPv4 only|Match DSCP values for IPv4 packets.|Valid values are from 0 to 63. Up to 8<br>comma-separated values can be entered.|
|QoSClassification -<br>Precedence|The packet IP precedence value must match one or<br>more precedence values.|A number from 0 to 7. Up to 8<br>comma-separated values can be entered.|
|QoSClassification -<br>Precedence - IPv4 only|Match precedence values for IPv4 packets.|A number from 0 to 7. Up to 8<br>comma-separated values can be entered.|



### p491_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager 7.0 User and Administrator Guide|Col2|Col3|

|Configure Devices|Col2|

||**Create a QoS Classification Profile**|



### p492_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Action|Description|Value|
|---|---|---|
|QoSClassification -<br>DEI|Drop eligible indicator (DEI) is used to indicate<br>frames eligible to be dropped when there is<br>congestion. The packet must match the DEI value<br>specified.|0 or 1.|
|QoS-Group|The packets must be permitted based on the selected<br>QoS group.|Up to 8 comma separated unique values<br>ranging from or 0-55 or 0-99 or 0-511<br>based on the selected device. Ensure that<br>the value you enter is supported on the<br>device.|
|QoSClassification -<br>Service Instance|Service Provider configurations have various<br>service instances on the Provider Edge (PE) routers.<br>QoS policy-maps are applied on these service<br>instances or group of service instances.<br>**Note**<br>This criteria is applicable only on Cisco ASR 903.|Accepts any number of comma separated<br>values ranging from 1-8000 and/or<br>hyphenated value with each ranging from<br>1-8000.|
|QoSClassification -<br>VLAN|Match and classify traffic on the basis of the virtual<br>local-area network (VLAN) identification number.<br>**Note**<br>Click the + icon to add more than one QOS<br>Classification - VLAN and specify values.|Accepts any number of comma separated<br>values ranging from 1-4095 and/or<br>hyphenated value with each ranging from<br>1-4095.|
|QoSClassification -<br>VLAN - Inner|Match and classify traffic on the basis of the inner<br>virtual local-area network (VLAN) identification<br>number.<br>**Note**<br>Click the + icon to add more than one QOS QOS<br>classifcation -VLAN- inner lines and specify<br>values.|Accepts any number of comma separated<br>values ranging from 1-4095 and/or<br>hyphenated value with each ranging from<br>1-4095.|
|QoSClassification -<br>Discard Class|Indicates that packets must be permitted/discarded<br>based on the selected discard class.|Accepted value is any number between<br>0-7.|
|QoSClassification -<br>Traffic Class|Traffic class of the QoS configuration.|Accepted value is any number between<br>0-7.|
