## Page 570

### p570_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Manage Circuits|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Service Details Reference**|



### p570_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Attribute|Description|
|---|---|
|Service Name|Unique name to identify the circuit/VC.|
|Service Description|Description of the VC that will help to identify the VC.|
|Service Type|Prepopulated based on the type of service you are creating—EPL, EVPL, EP-LAN, and so on.|
|Use EVPN|Enables you to create EVPN based connections.|
|Service MTU|The maximum size, in bytes, of any frame passing through the VC. Values can be between 64<br>to 65535. The service MTU must be lower than or equal to the MTU defined on all of the<br>service's UNIs. The service MTU value is always minimum of both endpoints MTU value.|
|Core Technology|VPLS or H-VPLS. See Core Technology for Multipoint EVCs, on page 495.<br>**Note**<br>For VPLS or H-VPLS, you can provision a maximum number of 20 devices using the<br>Provisioning Wizard.|
|VPN ID|Relevant for multipoint EVCs (both VPLS and H-VPLS). This field is automatically populated<br>with the next available pseudowire ID. This ID can be changed during the EVC creation process<br>(valid value range: 1-4294967295). The ID is not editable when modifying the EVC.<br>**Note**<br>The VPN ID is used uniquely across the network, meaning that two services will not use the<br>same VPN ID. In addition, the VPN ID cannot use a pseudowire ID which is already configured<br>in the network to avoid pseudowire ID collision. The VPN ID value is displayed in the PW<br>ID field.. You cannot modify the PW ID value for multipoint services during creation and<br>modification of services.|
|PW ID|Relevant for multipoint EVCs and point-to-point EVCs. This field is automatically populated<br>with the next available pseudowire ID. You can edit this ID to assign a value only in case of<br>point-to-point EVCs (valid value range: 1-4294967295) during the EVC creation process. The<br>ID is not editable when modifying the EVC.<br>**Note**<br>The PW ID is used uniquely across the network, meaning that two services will not use the<br>same PW ID.|
|Bundling|Enables multiple VLANs on this VC. Multiple CE-VLAN IDs are bundled to one EVC.|
|CE-VLAN ID Preservation|Ensures that the CE-VLAN ID of an egress service frame is identical in value to the CE-VLAN<br>ID of the corresponding ingress service frame. This must be enabled if bundling is enabled.|



### p570_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Col1|Col2|Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager 7.0 User and Administrator Guide|
|---|---|---|
|**530**|||



---

## Page 571

### p571_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Manage Circuits|Col2|
|---|---|
|**New UNI Details Reference**||



### p571_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Attribute|Description|
|---|---|
|CE-VLAN ID CoS Preservation|Ensures that the CE-VLAN CoS of an egress service frame is identical in value to the CE-VLAN<br>CoS of the corresponding ingress service frame. The CoS markings are unaltered.|



### p571_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Attribute|Description|
|---|---|
|MTU|The Maximum Transmission Size, in bytes, of a packet passing through the interface. The MTU of the<br>UNI must be greater than or equal to the MTU defined on the service level.|
|Auto Negotiation|Check this check box to automatically negotiate the speed and duplex mode.|
|Speed|Port speed. You can reduce the speed if this is supported on the port.<br>**Note**<br>This field is not available if you select the Auto Negotiation check box.|
|Duplex Mode|• Full Duplex—Uses simultaneous communication in both directions between the UNI and the customer’s<br>access switch, assuming that both sides support full duplex. If one side does not support full duplex,<br>the port will be brought down.<br>• Auto-Negotiation—Uses the mode that is agreed upon between the two devices, depending on what<br>is supported. Full Duplex will be attempted but if one device does not support it, half duplex will be<br>used.<br>**Note**<br>This field is not available if you select the Auto Negotiation check box.|
|Service Multiplexing|Allows the UNI to participate in more than one EVC instance.|
|UNI Allows Bundling|Allows the UNI to participate in VCs with Bundling enabled. See Bundling in Service Details Reference,<br>on page 530|
|Untagged CE-VLAN<br>ID|The ID of the CE-VLAN assigned to untagged traffic.|
|Ingress/Egress QoS<br>Profile|Select the required QoS profile for ingress or egress traffic on the UNI. The list of profiles includes policy<br>maps that were configured on the device and discovered by the system, as well as user-defined QoS profiles.|
|UNI QoS Profile|Applies a QoS profile on the UNI itself to define the bandwidth profile and other quality of service attributes<br>of the UNI. If you apply a QoS profile on the UNI level, you should not apply a QoS profile on the service<br>level.|
|Enable Link OAM|Enables IEEE 803.1ah link operation and maintenance. If Link OAM is enabled, you will see events relating<br>to the state of the link between this UNI and the customer’s access switch.|



### p571_default_t4 (default, high confidence)

|Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager 7.0 User and Administrator Guide|Col2|Col3|
|---|---|---|
|||**531**|

### p572_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Manage Circuits|Col2|
|---|---|
||**UNI Service Details Reference**|



### p572_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Attribute|Description|
|---|---|
|Enable Link<br>Management|Enables the customer access switch to get information about this UNI, VLAN IDs, services on the UNI,<br>and so on.|



### p572_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Attribute|Description|Additional Information|
|---|---|---|
|Ingress/Egress Service QoS<br>Profile|Select the required QoS profile for ingress or egress traffic on the UNI. The<br>list of profiles includes policy maps that were configured on the device and<br>discovered by the system and user-defined QoS profiles.||
|Layer 2 Control Protocol<br>Profile|Profile that determines how the various communication protocols are<br>handled. Frames using the various protocols are either tunneled, dropped,<br>or peered. Refer to MEF 6.1 for details.||
|Designation|For E-Tree: Select the role of the UNI in the VC, either Leaf or Root.||
|Use point to point connection<br>with Root|For E-Tree: If the UNI is designated as a leaf, you can select this check box<br>to create an active pseudowire between root and leaf. The check box will<br>not appear if there is more than one endpoint on a single device or if there<br>is more than one root in the service.||
|Match|Select the type of tagging the traffic should have in order to enter the UNI:<br>• Dot1q—Mapping of 802.1q frames ingress on an interface to the service<br>instance.<br>• Dot1ad—Mapping of 802.1ad frames ingress on an interface to the<br>service instance.<br>• Default—Traffic that is not assigned to any other VC on this port.<br>• Untagged—Frames that have no VLAN tag.||
|Auto Allocate VLAN|Check this check box to automatically allocate a VLAN ID for the UNI.||
|VLAN(s)|VLAN identifier, an integer 1–4094. You can enter a range of VLAN IDs<br>using a hyphen or a comma-separated series of VLAN IDs.|This field is not<br>available if you have<br>checked the Auto<br>Allocate VLAN check<br>box.|

## Page 573

### p573_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Manage Circuits|Col2|
|---|---|
|**Service OAM**||



### p573_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Attribute|Description|Additional Information|
|---|---|---|
|Inner VLAN(s)|VLAN identifier for the second level of VLAN tagging, an integer 1–4094.<br>You can enter a range of VLAN IDs using a hyphen or a comma-separated<br>series of VLAN IDs.||
|Untagged Bundled|Enables traffic with no VLAN tags to be bundled together with VLAN<br>tagged frames.||
|Priority Tagged Bundled|Enables priority tagged traffic to be bundled together with VLAN tagged<br>frames.||
|Exact|Prevents admittance of traffic with additional inner VLAN tags other than<br>those that are matched to be carried by the service.|Applicable for IOS-XR<br>devices only.|
|Outer VLAN CoS|The outer VLAN Class of Service identifier that should be associated with<br>the frame. The CoS ID can be an integer 0–7.|Applicable for IOS<br>devices only.|
|Inner VLAN CoS|The inner VLAN Class of Service identifier that should be associated with<br>the frame. The CoS ID can be an integer 0–7.|Applicable for IOS<br>devices only.|
|E-Type|Limits the service to only carry frames of the specified Ethertype:<br>• IPv4<br>• IPv6<br>• PPPoE-All<br>• PPPoE-Discovery<br>• PPPoE-Session|Applicable for IOS<br>devices only.|
|Rewrite Definition Action|The encapsulation adjustment to be performed when the frame enters the<br>UNI:<br>• None<br>• Pop—Removes one or two VLAN tags from the frame on ingress and<br>adds them on egress.<br>• Push—Adds one or two VLAN tags from the frame on ingress and<br>removes them on egress, either Dot1q or Dot1ad tags.<br>• Translate—Replaces VLAN tags with new VLAN tags, either Dot1q<br>or Dot1ad tags The translation can be 1:1, 1:2, 2:1, or 2:2.|The Translate action is<br>applicable for IOS-XR<br>devices only.|



### p573_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager 7.0 User and Administrator Guide|Col2|Col3|

|Metric Type|Choose the required Metric Type. The values are** IGP**,** Latency**,** TE**, and<br>**HopCount**.|

|New Segment List|Select the check box if you want to create a new segment list.|
|Segment List Name|This filed appears if New Segment List check box is selected.|
|Existing Segment List|This field appears if the New Segment List check box is not selected. Select a<br>segment list from the drop down list.|
|Weight|The weight range is from 1 to 4294967295.|
|**Note**<br>When entering the path details, you must click the** +** icon and provide the** Segment List Name** and** Weight**<br>to add details to the Segment list.<br>The Segments table is active for editing if the New Segment List check box is selected.<br>• You can add Segment by clicking +. Provide the** Index** value and select the** Device**,** Segment Type**,<br>and** Interface**from the respective drop down lists.<br>• If you have added multiple segments, you can place them in your desired queue by using the up or<br>down arrow in the segments window.<br>• You can also edit or delete a segment from the segments window only when you are creating it. Once<br>the segment list is created, it cannot be modified.<br>• You can also assign label for the interfaces which do not have label assigned to them.|**Note**<br>When entering the path details, you must click the** +** icon and provide the** Segment List Name** and** Weight**<br>to add details to the Segment list.<br>The Segments table is active for editing if the New Segment List check box is selected.<br>• You can add Segment by clicking +. Provide the** Index** value and select the** Device**,** Segment Type**,<br>and** Interface**from the respective drop down lists.<br>• If you have added multiple segments, you can place them in your desired queue by using the up or<br>down arrow in the segments window.<br>• You can also edit or delete a segment from the segments window only when you are creating it. Once<br>the segment list is created, it cannot be modified.<br>• You can also assign label for the interfaces which do not have label assigned to them.|
|Path Constraint Details|Path Constraint Details|
|Affinity Operation|Individually select the applicable affinity operations and specify the related details.<br>The values are** Exclude-Any**,** Include-Any**, and** Include-All**.|

### p587_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

### p587_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Attribute|Description|Enabled|

|Protection|Protection mechanism for the circuit. Cisco EPN Manager<br>supports the following protection mechanism based on the<br>circuit type selected:<br>• None—For unprotected circuits This value is available<br>for all OCH circuit types.<br>• PSM—When a Protection Switch Module (PSM) card is<br>connected to a TXP card. This value is available for<br>OCHNC WSON and OCHCC WSON circuit types.<br>• Y-Cable—When a transponder or muxponder card protects<br>the circuit. This value is available for OCHCC WSON<br>circuit type.<br>• Splitter—When a MXPP/TXPP card is used. The circuit<br>source and destination are on MXPP_MR_2.5G and<br>TXPP_MR_2.5G cards. These cards provide splitter<br>(line-level) protection (trunk protection typically on TXPP<br>or MXPP transponder cards). This value is available only<br>for OCHCC WSON circuit type.|For OCHNC WSON<br>circuit type.|
|**Route Properties**|**Route Properties**|**Route Properties**|
|Diverse From<br>Tunnel|Select a tunnel to ensure that it is not used by the circuit you<br>are provisioning. This is to ensure that if there is a failure in a<br>tunnel, the same tunnel is not used by another circuit.|For OCH-Trail UNI<br>circuit types when the<br>Mutual Diversity<br>check box is<br>unchecked.|
|Validation|Validation mode for the circuit. Values are:<br>• Full—The circuit is created when the circuit validation<br>result is greater than or equal to the acceptance threshold<br>value.<br>• None—The circuit is created without considering the<br>acceptance threshold value.|For all OCH circuit<br>types.|
|Acceptance<br>Threshold|Protection acceptance threshold value set for the OCH protected<br>circuits. Values are:<br>• Green—Indicates that the restoration failure risk is 0%.<br>• Yellow—Indicates that the restoration failure risk is<br>between 0% and 16%.<br>• Orange—Indicates that the restoration failure risk is<br>between 16% and 50%.<br>• Red—Indicates that the restoration failure risk is greater<br>that 50%.|For all OCH circuit<br>types when the<br>Validation field is set<br>to Full.|

|Service Type|Service types supported for the selected bandwidth.<br>See Table for the mapping of values in the Bandwidth and Service Type<br>fields.|For ODU UNI<br>circuit type.|

## Page 603

### p603_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Manage Circuits|Col2|
|---|---|
|**Endpoint Section Reference for OTN Circuit Types**||



### p603_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Attribute|Description|Enabled|
|---|---|---|
|Protection Type|Protection type for the OTN circuit. Values are:<br>• 1+0—Unprotected card. If a failure is detected in the working path,<br>it results in loss of data.<br>• 1+1—Both primary and secondary path carry traffic end to end and<br>the receiver receives and compares both the traffic. When the egress<br>node detects failure in one path, it switches the traffic to the<br>unaffected path.<br>• 1+R—When the primary path fails, the restored path is calculated<br>and traffic is switched to the restored path. If the primary path is<br>non-revertible, the restored path becomes the new primary path.<br>• 1+1+R—Both primary and secondary path carry traffic. When the<br>egress node detects failure in one path, it switches the traffic to the<br>unaffected path. The restored path is calculated and traffic is switched<br>to the restored path. If the primary or secondary path is non-revertible,<br>the restored path becomes the new primary or secondary path.<br>**Note**<br>This protection type is not supported for Cisco NCS 4000 series<br>devices.|For all OTN<br>circuit types<br>(except ODU<br>UNI Hairpin).|
|Diverse From<br>Tunnel ID|Select a tunnel to ensure that it is not used by the circuit you are<br>provisioning. This is to ensure that if there is a failure in a tunnel, the<br>same tunnel is not used by another circuit.|For all OTN<br>circuit<br>types(except<br>ODU UNI<br>Hairpin).|
|**Working Path**,**Protected Path**, and** Restored Path**<br>The Protected Path field group is available for all OTN circuit types (except ODU UNI Hairpin) only when<br>the Protection Type field is set to 1+1 or 1+1+R.<br>The Restored Path field group is available for all OTN circuit types (except ODU UNI Hairpin) only when<br>the Protection Type field is set to 1+R or 1+1+R.|**Working Path**,**Protected Path**, and** Restored Path**<br>The Protected Path field group is available for all OTN circuit types (except ODU UNI Hairpin) only when<br>the Protection Type field is set to 1+1 or 1+1+R.<br>The Restored Path field group is available for all OTN circuit types (except ODU UNI Hairpin) only when<br>the Protection Type field is set to 1+R or 1+1+R.|**Working Path**,**Protected Path**, and** Restored Path**<br>The Protected Path field group is available for all OTN circuit types (except ODU UNI Hairpin) only when<br>the Protection Type field is set to 1+1 or 1+1+R.<br>The Restored Path field group is available for all OTN circuit types (except ODU UNI Hairpin) only when<br>the Protection Type field is set to 1+R or 1+1+R.|
|Type|Choose the type of working path or protected path for the circuit. Values<br>are Dynamic and Explicit.|For all OTN<br>circuit types<br>(except ODU<br>UNI Hairpin).|
|New|Check this check box to create a new explicit working or protected path<br>for the circuit.|For all OTN<br>circuit types<br>(except ODU<br>UNI Hairpin)<br>when the Type<br>field is set to<br>Explicit.|

### p617_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|IP SLA Settings|IP SLA<br>Parameters|Descriptions|
|---|---|---|
|Operation<br>Settings|Name|Enter a unique name to identify the IP SLA operation for the selected L3VPN<br>service.|
|Operation<br>Settings|Type|Select the type of IP SLA operation that must be generated for the devices<br>participating in this L3VPN service. Your options are:<br>•** UDP Echo**: Configures an IP SLAs User Datagram Protocol (UDP) Echo<br>operation to measure response times and to test end-to-end connectivity between<br>a Cisco device and devices using IPv4 or IPv6.<br>•** ICMP Echo**: Allows you to measure end-to-end network response time<br>between a Cisco device and other devices (source and destination values, as<br>described below) using IPv4 or IPv6. With an IP SLA operation of type ICPM<br>Echo, you cannot associate the 'Connection Loss' action variable.<br>•** UDP Jitter**: Configures the UDP jitter operation which analyzes round-trip<br>delay, one-way delay, one-way jitter, one-way packet loss, and connectivity<br>in networks that carry UDP traffic in IPv4 or IPv6 networks.|
|Operation<br>Settings|Source|Specify the device which acts as the source point from which the IP SLA<br>configuration is generated. The IP SLA responses are generated based on the<br>connectivity between this source device and the target device. The VRF values for<br>this operation are automatically selected based on your Source selection.|
|Operation<br>Settings|Source Port|Enter a numeric value between 0 and 65535 to specify the source port value for<br>which the IP SLA operation must be configured.|
|Operation<br>Settings|Destination|Specify the device which acts as the target point from which the IP SLA<br>configuration is generated. The IP SLA responses are generated based on the<br>connectivity between the source device and this target device.|
|Operation<br>Settings|Destination<br>Port|Enter a numeric value between 0 and 65535 to specify the destination port value<br>for which the IP SLA operation must be generated.|
|Operation<br>Settings|VRF|The VRF details are automatically selected based on the device that you specify as<br>the IP SLA operation Source.|

### p618_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|IP SLA Settings|IP SLA<br>Parameters|Descriptions|
|---|---|---|
|Reaction<br>Settings|Action<br>Variable|Select the variable based on which the IP SLA reactions must be triggered. For<br>example, when a monitored value exceeds or falls below a specified level, or when<br>a monitored event (such as a timeout or connection loss) occurs.<br>•** Connection Loss**: Indicates that an event must be triggered when a connection<br>loss occurs. This value is not displayed if you select ICPM Echo as the type<br>of operation.<br>•** Round Trip Time**: If you choose this action variable, you must enter the<br>**Upper Threshold Value** and the** Lower Threshold Value** which indicates<br>that an event must be triggered when a monitored value exceeds or falls below<br>the upper and lower threshold values that you specify.<br>•** Time Out**: Indicates that an event must be triggered after a given set of<br>consecutive timeouts occur.<br>•** Verify Error**: Indicates that an event must be triggered after an error of type<br>'VerifyError' occurs.|
|Reaction<br>Settings|Action Type|Select one of the following actions that must be taken based on the conditions set<br>in the Action Variable field:<br>•** None**: No action is taken.<br>•** Trap and Trigger**: Triggers both an SNMP trap and starts another IP SLAs<br>operation when the violation conditions are met, as defined in the Trap Only<br>and Trigger Only options below.<br>•** Trap Only**: Sends an SNMP logging trap when the specified violation type<br>occurs for the monitored element.<br>•** Trigger Only**: Changes the state of one or more target operation's Operational<br>state from 'pending' to 'active' when the violation conditions are met. A target<br>operation continues until its life expires (as specified by the target operation's<br>configured lifetime value). A triggered target operation must finish its life<br>before it can be triggered again.|
|Reaction<br>Settings|Threshold<br>Type||

### p619_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|IP SLA Settings|IP SLA<br>Parameters|Descriptions|
|---|---|---|
|||Select the threshold type based on which the IP SLA events are generated.<br>•** Average**: If you choose this threshold type, enter the** N Value** which specifies<br>that an event must be triggered when the averaged total value of N probes is<br>reached either when specified upper-threshold value is exceeded, or when it<br>falls below the lower-threshold value.<br>•** Consecutive**: If you choose this threshold type, enter the** Consecutive Values**<br>as part of the reaction settings. This threshold type triggers an event only after<br>a violation occurs a specified number of times consecutively. For example, if<br>you enter 5 as the consecutive value, the consecutive violation type is used to<br>configure an action to occur after a timeout occurs 5 times in a row, or when<br>the round-trip-time exceeds the upper threshold value 5 times in a row.<br>•** Immediate**: Triggers an event immediately when the value for a reaction type<br>(such as response time) exceeds the upper threshold value or falls below the<br>lower threshold value, or when a timeout, connection loss, or verify that error<br>event occurs.<br>•** Never**: Never triggers an event.<br>•** X out of Y occurrences**: If you choose this threshold type, enter the** X Values**<br>and** Y Values** to specify the number of occurrences. This triggers an event<br>after some number (x) of violations within some other number (y) of probe<br>operations (x of y).|
|Simple Schedule|-|Enter the scheduling parameters for an individual IP SLAs operation by entering<br>the following values:<br>•** Frequency**: Enter the elapsed time within which the operation must repeat,<br>in seconds.<br>•** Life Time**: Enter the overall time until when the operation must be active, in<br>seconds. A single operation repeats at the specified frequency for the lifetime<br>of the operation.<br>•** Age Out**: Enter the length of time to keep an operation active, in seconds. For<br>example, an age out value of 43200 will ensure that the operation will age out<br>after 12 hours of inactivity.<br>•** Start Now** and** Start After**: Enable the Start Now check box to schedule the<br>IP SLA operation to be executed immediately on Save. Or use the Start After<br>field to specify the number of minutes after which the operation can be<br>executed.|

## Page 623

### p623_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Manage Circuits|Col2|
|---|---|
|**PE-CE Authentication**||



### p623_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Attribute|Description|
|---|---|
|Router ID|Specify an IPv4 address for the OSPF protocol.|
|Area ID|Define an area for the OSPF protocol. The valid range is 0 to 4294967295.|
|Metric|Specify a numeric value for the OSPF protocol.|
|Domain Type|Select the required domain type.|
|Domain Value|Enter the domain value in the 6 Octet Hexadecimal format. For example,<br>00000000000F.|
|BFD Min Interval|Enter the minimum interval between which control packets are sent to the<br>neighbor. The range is 3–30000 milliseconds.|
|BFD Min Rx|Enter the minimum Rx value. The range is 3–30000 milliseconds.|
|BFD Multiplier|The multiplier is the number of times a packet is missed before BFD declares the<br>neighbor down. The range for the OSPF protocol is 2–50 for Cisco IOS-XR and<br>3–50 for Cisco IOS-XR devices.|
|BFD Fast Detect|Check this check box to quickly detect failures in the path between adjacent<br>forwarding engines.|

|**Working Path and Protecting Path**|**Working Path and Protecting Path**|
|Port Name or Interface<br>Name|Name of the interface on the source and destination devices in the CEM service.<br>You can choose either the port name or the port group.<br>When you choose the port name under the** Protecting Path** area, the unidirectional<br>path switched ring (UPSR) protection mechanism is enabled.<br>When you choose the port group under the** Protecting Path** area, the Automatic<br>Protection Switching (APS) protection mechanism is enabled. For more<br>information about how to configure protection groups, see Configure APS or<br>MSP and UPSR or SNCP Protection Groups, on page 336.|
|Higher Order Path|When a SONET/SDH line is channelized, it is logically divided into smaller<br>bandwidth channels called higher order paths (HOP) and lower order paths (LOP).<br>HOP or synchronous transport signal (STS) path is used to transport TDM data<br>of higher bandwidth. HOPs can also contain LOPs within it.<br>Select the path and path mode available for the CEM service.|
|Lower Order Path|LOPs or virtual tributary (VT) path is used to transport TDM data of lower<br>bandwidth.|
|DS0 Time Slot|Choose one or more time slots available in the DS0 group.<br>**Note**<br>This field is available only if you select** DS0** in the** Service Type** field.|
|**Clocking**<br>The nodes in a network may be at different clock rates. Differences in timing at nodes may cause the receiving<br>node to either drop or reread information sent to it. Clocking is essential to synchronize all nodes to the same<br>clock rate. For more information about clocking, see Configure Clocking for CEM, on page 339.|**Clocking**<br>The nodes in a network may be at different clock rates. Differences in timing at nodes may cause the receiving<br>node to either drop or reread information sent to it. Clocking is essential to synchronize all nodes to the same<br>clock rate. For more information about clocking, see Configure Clocking for CEM, on page 339.|

### p634_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Manage Circuits|Col2|

||**CEM Service Details References**|



### p634_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Attribute|Description|
|---|---|
|Clock Source|Enables to recover the clock rate from single source so that all nodes can be<br>synchronized at the same clock rate. Values are:<br>• Internal – Clock rate recovered from the host.<br>• Line – Clock rate recovered from the SONET/SDH line.<br>• Adaptive Clock Recovery – Clock rate is recovered based on the dejitter<br>buffer fill level. Due to delay variations, the dejitter buffer fill levels keep<br>varying continuously. The TDM service clock is recovered after filtering<br>the variations. The accuracy of the recovered clock depends on the delay<br>variations.<br>• Differential Clock Recovery – Clock rate is recovered from a primary clock<br>using Sync-E. For more information about how to setup the primary clock<br>for your network, see Synchronize the Clock Using Sync-E, BITS, and PTP,<br>on page 350.<br>**Note**<br>Cisco IOS-XE devices running version 17.9.5 or higher support adaptive and<br>differential clock recovery (ACR/DCR) and SAToP framing for DS1 and DS3<br>services over STS1E controllers.|
|**QOS**<br>The list of profiles available for selection includes policy maps that were configured on the device and<br>discovered by the system, as well as user-defined QoS profiles.|**QOS**<br>The list of profiles available for selection includes policy maps that were configured on the device and<br>discovered by the system, as well as user-defined QoS profiles.|
|Ingress QoS Profile|Select the ingress QoS policies that are configured on the A end and Z end devices.|
|**Unmanaged Device Details**<br>**Note**<br>The below fields are available only for Z End Configurations.|**Unmanaged Device Details**<br>**Note**<br>The below fields are available only for Z End Configurations.|
|Unmanaged Device|Check this check box to include a device that is not managed by Cisco EPN<br>Manager and create partial service.|
|New Device|Check this check box to create a new unmanaged device.|
|Device|Choose an unmanaged device from the drop-down list.<br>**Note**<br>This field is available only when the** New Device** check box is unchecked.|
|Device Name|Enter a unique name for the new unmanaged device that you want to create.<br>**Note**<br>This field is available only when the** New Device** check box is checked. |Idle pattern|Idle pattern to transmit the data when the service goes down. The valid range is<br>0x00 - 0xFF.|
|Dummy Mode|Enables you to set a bit pattern for filling in for lost or corrupted frames. The<br>values are last-frame and user-defined.|

|RTP Header Enabled|Check this check box to enable the Real-Time Transport Protocol (RTP) header<br>for the CEM service.|
|RTP Compression<br>Enabled|Check this check box to compress the IP header in a packet before the packet is<br>transmitted. It reduces network overhead and speeds up the transmission of RTP.|
|**Pseudowire Settings**|**Pseudowire Settings**|

## Page 650

### p650_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Manage Circuits|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Field References for Tunnel Creation—MPLS TE Tunnel**|



### p650_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Attribute|Description|
|---|---|
|Enable Autoroute|Check this check box to enable autoroute for the tunnel.|
|Enable BFD Settings|Check this check box to enable the Bidirectional Forwarding Detection (BFD)<br>protocol. BFD provides fast forwarding path failure detection time and a consistent<br>failure detection method.|
|Protection Type|Choose one of the following protection mechanisms for the TE tunnel:<br>• Working—The tunnel has only a working path.<br>• Working+Protected—The tunnel has a working and a protected path, wherein<br>if the working path fails, the traffic flow is automatically routed to the<br>protected path without the links going down.<br>• Working+Restore—The tunnel has a working and a restore path, wherein<br>if the working path fails, the link goes down and then the traffic flow is<br>routed to the restore path.<br>• Working+Protected+Restore—The tunnel has a working, protected, and<br>restore path, wherein, if the working path fails, the traffic flow is routed to<br>the protected path. If the protected path also fails, the link goes down and<br>then the traffic flow is routed to the restore path.|
|Deployment Action|Choose one of the following options to specify what happens when the MPLS<br>TE tunnel creation process is completed:<br>• Preview—Previews the configurations that will be deployed to the relevant<br>devices before the actual deployment.<br>• Deploy—Deploys the configurations immediately upon completion.|

## Page 651

### p651_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Manage Circuits|Col2|
|---|---|
|**Field References for Tunnel Creation—MPLS TE Tunnel**||



### p651_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Attribute|Description|
|---|---|
|**Tunnel Setting**|**Tunnel Setting**|
|Global ID|The global ID assigned to both, source and destination endpoints. This ID must<br>be the same to bind two unidirectional tunnels into a bidirectional TE tunnel. The<br>default value is 0.<br>**Note**<br>This attribute is available only when you create a bidirectional TE tunnel. EPNM<br>supports a global id only within the range of 1–2147483647.|
|Affinity Bits|The affinity bit determines the link attribute that the bidirectional TE tunnel uses<br>when configuring the dynamic backup paths.|
|Affinity Mask|The affinity mask determines which link attributes the router must check.<br>You can use affinity bits and affinity mask to include or exclude link attributes<br>when configuring the dynamic backup paths. If a bit in the mask is 0, the value<br>of the associated link attribute for that bit is irrelevant. In this case, the link<br>attribute is excluded when configuring the dynamic backup paths. If a bit in the<br>mask is 1, the value of the associated link attribute must match the affinity of the<br>tunnel for that bit. In this case, the link attribute is included when configuring<br>the dynamic backup paths.|
|Setup Priority|Setup priority assigned to an LSP for the unidirectional or bidirectional TE tunnels.<br>Based on this priority, the LSP can determine which existing tunnels or LSPs<br>with low priority can be blocked.<br>Valid values are 0–7. A lower number indicates a higher priority. For example,<br>an LSP with a setup priority of 0 can block any LSP with a setup priority 1–7.<br>**Note**<br>Setup priority cannot be higher than the hold priority.|
|Hold Priority|Hold priority assigned to an LSP for the unidirectional or bidirectional TE tunnels.<br>Based on this priority, the LSP can determine whether it must be blocked by<br>another signaling LSP with a high setup priority.<br>Valid values are 0–7. A lower number indicates a higher priority. For example,<br>an LSP with a hold priority of 0 cannot be blocked by another LSP.|
|Bandwidth Pool Type|Bandwidth pool used to manage the reservable bandwidth on each link for<br>constraint-based routing (CBR) in MPLS TE. Values are:<br>• Global – Regular TE tunnel bandwidth<br>• Subpool – A portion of the global pool. The subpool bandwidth is not<br>reserved from the global pool if it is not in use. Subpool tunnels require a<br>higher priority than global pool tunnels.<br>**Note**<br>This field is available only when you uncheck the** Enable Auto Bandwidth**<br>check box.|



### p651_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager 7.0 User and Administrator Guide|Col2|Col3|
|---|---|---|

### p652_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Manage Circuits|Col2|

||**Field References for Tunnel Creation—MPLS TE Tunnel**|



### p652_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Attribute|Description|
|---|---|
|Bandwidth|Bandwidth for the bidirectional TE tunnel. You can choose the unit of the<br>bandwidth from the drop-down list. The available units are Kbps, Mbps, and<br>Gbps.<br>For example, if you want to assign a bandwidth of 1000000 Kbps for the tunnel,<br>enter the value as 1000 Gbps.<br>**Note**<br>This field is available only when you uncheck the** Enable Auto Bandwidth**<br>check box.|
|Auto Bandwidth Max|Cisco EPN Manager automatically assigns the maximum bandwidth for the TE<br>tunnel based on the traffic. However, you can change the bandwidth if required.<br>You can choose the unit of the bandwidth from the drop-down list. The available<br>units are Kbps, Mbps, and Gbps.<br>**Note**<br>This field is available only when you check the** Enable Auto Bandwidth** check<br>box in the** Customer Service Detail** screen.|
|Auto Bandwidth Min|Cisco EPN Manager automatically assigns the minimum bandwidth for the TE<br>tunnel based on the traffic. However, you can change the bandwidth, if required.<br>You can choose the unit of the bandwidth from the drop-down list. The available<br>units are Kbps, Mbps, and Gbps.<br>**Note**<br>This field is available only when you check the** Enable Auto Bandwidth** check<br>box in the** Customer Service Detail** screen.|
|Bandwidth Change<br>Frequency (Sec)|Enter the bandwidth change frequency in seconds. The valid range is 300–604800.<br>**Note**<br>This field is available only when you check the** Enable Auto Bandwidth** check<br>box in the** Customer Service Detail** page when you create tunnels.|
|Adjustment Threshold|Enter the bandwidth adjustment threshold in percentage to trigger an adjustment<br>if the largest sample percentage is higher or lower than the current tunnel<br>bandwidth. Adjustment threshold is the percentage of the current tunnel bandwidth<br>and an absolute (minimum) bandwidth. Both the thresholds must be fulfilled for<br>the automatic bandwidth to resignal the tunnel. The tunnel bandwidth is adjusted<br>if the difference between the largest sample output rate and the current tunnel<br>bandwidth is larger than the adjustment thresholds.<br>The valid range for the tunnels that connect the Cisco IOS-XR devices is 1–100.<br>The range for the tunnels that connect the Cisco IOS-XE devices is 1–99.<br>**Note**<br>This field is available only when you check the** Enable Auto Bandwidth** check<br>box in the** Customer Service Detail** page when you create tunnels.|

### p653_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Overflow Threshold|Enter the overflow threshold in percentage to trigger the overflow detection. It<br>is the percentage of the actual signaled tunnel bandwidth. An overflow detection<br>is triggered if the difference between measured bandwidth and actual bandwidth<br>is larger than overflow threshold percentage for N consecutive times. This is also<br>known as the overflow limit.<br>The valid range for the tunnels that connect the Cisco IOS-XR devices is 1–100<br>and the range for the tunnels that connect the Cisco IOS-XE devices is 1–99.<br>**Note**<br>This field is available only when you check the** Enable Auto Bandwidth** check<br>box in the** Customer Service Detail** page when you create tunnels.|
|Overflow Limit|Enter the number of consecutive collection periods during which the difference<br>between the measured bandwidth and the actual bandwidth of a tunnel can exceed<br>the overflow threshold defined for the tunnel.<br>The valid range is 1–10.<br>**Note**<br>This field is available only when you check the** Enable Auto Bandwidth** check<br>box in the** Customer Service Detail** page when you create tunnels.|

|**BFD Settings**|**BFD Settings**|
|New BFD|This checkbox is selected by default when you select the** Enable BFD Settings**<br>checkbox. Allows you to create a new BFD template for both bidirectional (Flex<br>LSP) and unidirectional tunnels during provisioning.|
|BFD Template Name|Enter the name for the new BFD template.|
|BFD Template|Displays the selected BFD template name by concatenating the device name. For<br>example, from A-End and/or Z-End devices. Choose an existing template from<br>the existing template name and the related Min Interval and Multiplier range<br>values are displayed by default.<br>Alphabets, digits, and special characters _(underscore),-(hyphen),.(dot) are<br>allowed, and BFD Template name should be fewer than 32 characters long.<br>The BFD template name should not have .(dots) or digits or combination of digits<br>and .(dots).<br>**Note**<br>This field is available only when you clear the** New BFD** checkbox.|

|Attribute|Description|
|---|---|
|Device Name|Enter a unique name for the new unmanaged device that you want to create.<br>**Note**<br>This field is available as a drop-down list if you have unchecked the** New Device**<br>check box. You can choose an unmanaged device as your Z endpoint.|
|Device IP|Enter the IP address of the new unmanaged device that you want to create.<br>**Note**<br>This field is available only when the** New Device** check box is checked. If the<br>**New Device** check box is unchecked, the IP address of the unmanaged device<br>that you chose in the** Device** drop-down list is populated in this field.|
|LDP IP|Enter a valid LDP IP for the unmanaged device.|
|VC ID|Enter a unique Virtual Circuit (VC) ID for the unmanaged device.|
|**Line Settings**|**Line Settings**|
|Speed|The speed of the serial link in kilo bits per second.|
|Data Bits|The measurement of actual data per packet that is transmitted through the serial<br>circuit/VC. The values are 5, 6, 7, and 8.|
|Stop Bits|Indicates the end of communication for a single packet. The values are 1, 1.5,<br>and 2 bits.<br>Since the data is clocked across the lines and each device has its own clock, it is<br>possible for the two devices to become slightly out of sync. Therefore, the stop<br>bits not only indicate the end of transmission but also provides the network with<br>some lenience to synchronize the different clocks. The more bits that are used<br>for stop bits, the greater the lenience in synchronizing the different clocks, but<br>slower the data transmission rate.|



### p662_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Col1|Col2|Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager 7.0 User and Administrator Guide|
|---|---|---|
|**622**|||



---

## Page 663

### p663_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Manage Circuits|Col2|
|---|---|
|**Serial Service Details Reference**||



### p663_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Attribute|Description|
|---|---|
|Parity|Used to check errors in serial communication. The values are:<br>• None—No parity defined for the circuit/VC.<br>• Even— The serial port will set the parity bit (the last bit after the data bits)<br>to a value to ensure that the transmission has an even number of logic high<br>bits. For example, if the data was 011, then for even parity, the parity bit<br>would be 0 to keep the number of logic high bits even.<br>• Odd— The serial port will set the parity bit (the last bit after the data bits)<br>to a value to ensure that the transmission has an odd number of logic high<br>bits. For example, if the data was 011, then for odd parity, the parity bit<br>would be 1, resulting in 3 logic high bits.<br>• Mark— Sets the parity bit high. This allows the receiving device to know<br>the state of a bit which enables the device to determine if noise is corrupting<br>the data or if the transmitting and receiving devices' clocks are out of sync.<br>• Space—Sets the parity bit low. This allows the receiving device to know<br>the state of a bit which enables the device to determine if noise is corrupting<br>the data or if the transmitting and receiving devices' clocks are out of sync.|
|Duplex Mode|Choose the required duplex mode for the serial service from the following options:<br>• HalfDuplex—Supports communication in both directions between the<br>endpoints, but not simultaneously. The transmission of data happens at one<br>direction at a time.<br>• FullDuplex—Supports simultaneous communication in both directions<br>between the endpoints assuming that both endpoints support full duplex. If<br>one side does not support full duplex, the port will be brought down.<br>**Note**<br>This field is available only for RS485 and RS422 service types. You can edit<br>RS485 and RS422 service type details. This is because you can select Duplex<br>mode between Half and Full for RS485 and RS422. However, you cannot edit<br>RS232 service type details because for RS232 you can select only FULL Duplex<br>mode.|
|**Pseudowire Settings**|**Pseudowire Settings**|
|Preferred Path Type|Choose the Preferred Path Type as Bidirectional or Unidirectional.|
|Preferred Path|Select the MPLS bidirectional TE tunnel through which you want the serial<br>service to pass through.<br>**Note**<br>This field is available only if you selected** Bidirectional** as the Preferred Path<br>Type.|



### p663_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager 7.0 User and Administrator Guide|Col2|Col3|

||**Raw Socket Service Details Reference**|



### p666_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Attribute|Description|
|---|---|
|Port Name|Name of the interface on the server and client devices in the Raw Socket service.|
|Server Address and<br>Server Port|The IP address and the port number of the server.|
|Allowed Sessions|To preconfigure a limit on the number of TCP raw-socket sessions per interface.<br>Its default value is 32.|
|Client Address and Client<br>Port|The IP address and the port number of the client.|
|Connection Idle Timeout|TCP session timeout setting for the Raw Socket service. If no data is transferred<br>between the client and server over this interval, then the TCP session closes. The<br>client then automatically attempts to reestablish the TCP session with the server.|
|VRF|Virtual Routing and Forwarding (VRF) interface through which the server and<br>client are connected to transport the data.<br>**Note**<br>Ensure that the VRF definition is common for both server and client.|
|Speed|The speed of the serial link in kilo bits per second. This line setting is optional<br>for Sync service settings.|
|Data Bits|The measurement of actual data per packet that is transmitted through the serial<br>circuit/VC. The values are 5, 6, 7, and 8. This line setting is optional for Sync<br>service settings.|
|Stop Bits|Indicates the end of communication for a single packet. The values are 1, 1.5,<br>and 2 bits. This line setting is optional for Sync service settings.|
|Parity|Checks errors in serial communication. This line setting is optional for Sync<br>service settings.|
|Duplex Mode|The duplex mode for the selected serial service. This line setting is optional for<br>Sync service settings.|
|DTR|Choose one of the following options:<br>• Used—Allows you to configure Data Terminal Ready (DTR) equipment<br>from the customer end if there are no connected cables.<br>• Not Used—Allows you not to configure Data Terminal Ready (DTR)<br>equipment from the customer end if there are no connected cables.<br>**Note**<br>This option is available only if the SyncRS232 check box is selected.|
|Clock Rate|Choose the desired clock rate in bits per second (bps) for the service. The valid<br>values are 48000 and 64000.|
|NRZI Encoding|Check this check box to enable the nonreturn-to-zero inverted (NRZI) encoding<br>mechanism for the service.|

|Packet Length|The packet length that triggers the routing device (either a server or a client) to<br>transmit the serial data to the peer. When the device collects the specified bytes<br>of data in its buffer, it packetizes the accumulated data and forwards it to the Raw<br>Socket peer.|
|Fragment Off|Check this check box to disable the frame relay fragmentation for this service.|
|Packet Timer|Specifies the amount of time in milliseconds, the device (either server or client)<br>waits to receive the next character in a stream. If a character is not received by<br>the time the packet timer expires, the data the device has accumulated in its buffer<br>is packetized and forwarded to the Raw Socket peer.|
|Special Char|A character that triggers the device (either server or client) to packetize the data<br>accumulated in its buffer and send it to the Raw Socket peer. When the specified<br>special character is received, the device packetizes the accumulated data and<br>sends it to the Raw Socket peer.|

### p681_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Circuit or VC<br>Serviceability<br>State|Icon|Description|
|---|---|---|
|Admin Down||Circuit or VC manually shutdown by the administrator.|
|Down||Circuit or VC is operationally down and administratively up.|
|Up||Circuit or VC is operationally and administratively up.|
|Auto Up||Circuit or VC is operationally auto up and administratively up. Only certain<br>devices support the Auto Up operational state.|
|Unavailable||Circuit or VC has not been discovered yet, or its operational status is<br>unavailable.|
|Partial||Circuit/VC operational or administrative state is partial.<br>• Partial admin state—The circuit or VC has a mixed administrative<br>request (to activate some service resources and deactivate others), has<br>a mix of resources that are administratively up and down, or has<br>resources whose operational state is unavailable.<br>• Partial operational state—The circuit or VC has a mix of some active<br>and deactivated resources, or the operational state for some of its<br>resources are unavailable.|
|Up -<br>Unprotected||The circuit/VC that was configured with a protection path is operational but<br>cannot switch to the alternate path because of severe failures.<br>**Note**<br>This serviceability status indication is supported for OCHCC WSON circuits<br>with Y-Cable protection and protected ODU.|

### p690_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Information<br>Provided in<br>Circuit/VC 360 View|Description|
|---|---|
|General information|Type of circuit/VC, its various states (discovery, serviceability, provisioning), the<br>customer associated with the circuit/VC, and some audit information (when it was<br>created, when it was last changed). For an explanation of circuit/VC states, see<br>Circuit or VC States, on page 640.<br>**Note**<br>If the Provisioning State is** Create Failed**, click the associated_ i_ (**information**) icon<br>to see the reason for the failure.<br>Auto-Refresh— For real-time updates of status and troubleshooting, enable an<br>on-demand refresh by clicking on the** Refresh** icon. Alternatively, you can also set<br>the auto-refresh interval to 30 seconds, 1 minute, 2 minutes or 5 minutes from the<br>drop-down list. Auto-Refresh is OFF by default.<br>**Note**<br>The Auto-Refresh setting is applicable only for the currently open 360 view popup<br>window. If the view is closed and reopened or another view is opened, by default<br>Auto-Refresh remains Off.<br>The reserved bandwidth utilization of the TE tunnel is displayed based on the<br>bandwidth configured on the tunnel compared to the bandwidth configured on the<br>Pseudowire associated to the tunnel.|
|Performance data|Graphs reflecting various aspects of the circuit/VC performance.<br>**Note**<br>For data to be shown in the graphs, the required monitoring policy must be activated<br>for the relevant devices. For example, to view graphs that chart the number of<br>Explicit Pointer Adjustment Relay counters (such L-bits and P-bits) that have been<br>generated and received, both the CEM and Pseudowire Emulation Edge to Edge<br>monitoring policies must be enabled. See Monitoring Policies Reference, on page<br>985.|
|Alarms|Current alarms for the circuit/VC, including their severity, status, and the time they<br>were generated.|
|Endpoints|Devices and interfaces that serve as endpoints for this circuit/VC.|
|EVIs|This tab displays the EVI endpoints. The** EVI Details** tab displays the EVI details,<br>route targets, and route policies configured for the selected endpoints.|

## Page 710

### p710_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Manage Circuits|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Initiate a Protection Switch Action on a Circuit (Optical)**|



### p710_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Protection Switch<br>Action|Description|Applicable when:|
|---|---|---|
|Force On Working|Configures the working path to carry<br>traffic over the network.|The current state of the protection switch<br>action is 'Manual On Protect' or 'Manual<br>On Working'.|
|Manual On Protect|Switches the traffic manually from the<br>working to the protected path.|There is no protection switch action<br>initiated on the circuit.|
|Clear|Clears the protection switch state on<br>the circuit.|The current state of the protection switch<br>action is not 'Lockout On Working'.|
|Exercise|Checks if an ODU subcontroller is<br>ready for a protection switch.|There is no protection switch action<br>initiated on the circuit.|



### p710_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Col1|Col2|Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager 7.0 User and Administrator Guide|
|---|---|---|
|**670**|||

## Page 711

### p711_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Manage Circuits|Col2|
|---|---|
|**Resynchronize a Circuit/VC**||



### p711_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Manual On Working|Switches the traffic manually from the<br>protected path to the working path.|There is no protection switch action<br>initiated on the circuit.|
|---|---|---|
|Lockout On Working|Configures an ODUk subcontroller as<br>a locked out resource in the ODU<br>subcontroller group. Locks the circuit<br>so that its traffic cannot be switched<br>to the working path.|The current state of the protection switch<br>action is not 'Lockout On Working'.|
|Clear Lock out|Clears the 'Lockout On Working'<br>switch state for the circuit.|The current state of the protection switch<br>action is 'Lockout On Working'.|
|Status|Displays the details of ODU<br>subcontroller group and the protection<br>switch state specified in the AID.|Available for all protected optical circuits.|
|Force On Protect|Configures the protected path to carry<br>traffic over the network.|The current state of the protection switch<br>action is 'Manual On Protect' or 'Manual<br>On Working'.|

## Page 726

### p726_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Manage Circuits|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Perform a Ping or Traceroute Using OAM Command**|



### p726_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Technology Type|Launched from Alarm Browser|Launched from Service/Circuit 360|
|---|---|---|
|LSP|From the** Destination LDP ID**<br>drop-down list, choose the LDP ID<br>of the destination endpoint<br>participating in the service.|Specify the** Source** and** Destination** from<br>the drop-down lists.<br>In the** Destination** field,<br>• If a LDP enabled device is selected,<br>then Ping and Traceroute options are<br>enabled.<br>• If SR enabled device is selected, then<br>Ping, Traceroute, Multipath, Nil FEC<br>Ping and Nil FEC Traceroute options<br>are enabled. (Nil FEC options are<br>enabled only if Label,<br>OutputInterface and NextHop fields<br>are populated)|
|MPLS Bidirectional TE Tunnel (Flex<br>LSP)|Choose the tunnel's path as** Active**,<br>**Working**, or** Path-Protect** for<br>which you want to perform a ping<br>or traceroute. Cisco EPN Manager<br>performs the ping or traceroute on<br>both directions, that is, from<br>headend to tailend and vice versa.|Choose the tunnel's path as** Active**,<br>**Working**, or** Path-Protect** for which you<br>want to perform a ping or traceroute.<br>Cisco EPN Manager performs the ping or<br>traceroute on both directions, that is, from<br>headend to tailend and vice versa.|
|VRF in L3VPN|From the** End Points** drop-down<br>list, choose the endpoint of another<br>VRF that belongs to the same VPN.|From the** Source End Points** and<br>**Destination End Points** drop-down lists,<br>choose the source and destination<br>endpoints of another VRF that belongs to<br>the same VPN.|
|CFM in Carrier Ethernet|From the** Destination MEP ID**<br>drop-down list, choose the MEP ID<br>of the destination endpoint<br>participating in the service.|From the** Source MEP ID** and<br>**Destination MEP ID** drop-down lists,<br>choose the MEP IDs of the source and<br>destination endpoints participating in the<br>service.|
|SR TE||From the** Policy Name** drop-down list,<br>choose a policy.<br>Note: This option is enabled for devices<br>configured over static and dynamic SR<br>policies or EVPN technology.|

|BERT Pattern|Description|
|---|---|
|2^11|Pseudo-random repeating test pattern that consists of 2,048 bits.|
|2^15|Pseudo-random repeating test pattern that consists of 32,767 bits.|
|2^20-O151|Pseudo-random repeating test pattern that consists of 1,048,575 bits.|
|2^20-O153|Pseudo-random repeating test pattern that consists of 1,048,575 bits.|
|2^23|Pseudo-random 0.151 test pattern that is 8,388,607 bits in length.|
|2^9|Pseudo-random 0.151 test pattern that is 511 bits in length.|



### p734_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Col1|Col2|Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager 7.0 User and Administrator Guide|
|---|---|---|
|**694**|||

|---|---|
|**Use Traditional Licensing**||



### p767_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|License<br>Registration Status|Description|
|---|---|
|Unregistered|Smart Software Licensing is enabled in Cisco EPN Manager but Cisco EPN Manager<br>is not registered with the CSSM.|
|Registered|Cisco EPN Manager is registered with the CSSM. Cisco EPN Manager has received<br>an ID certificate that will be used for future communication with the Cisco licensing<br>authority.|
|Registration<br>Expired|Cisco EPN Manager did not successfully renew its registration prior to the expiration<br>date and has been removed from CSSM.|



### p767_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|License<br>Authorization<br>Status|Description|
|---|---|
|Evaluation Mode|Cisco EPN Manager is running in evaluation mode (expires in 90 days).|
|Authorized|Cisco EPN Manager has a valid Smart Account and is registered. All licenses requested<br>by the product are authorized for use.|
|Out of Compliance|Cisco EPN Manager has exceeded the number of licenses that were purchased.<br>(Specifically, the virtual account for the product instance has a shortage of one or more<br>licenses types.)|
|Evaluation Expired|The evaluation period has expired and Cisco EPN Manager is in the unlicensed state.|
|Authorization<br>Expired|Cisco EPN Manager did not successfully renew its license authorization prior to the<br>authorization expiration date.|

## Page 777

### p777_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Administer the Cisco EPN Manager System|Col2|
|---|---|
|**Ports Used by Cisco EPN Manager**||



### p777_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Port|Protocol|Usage|Safe to<br>Disable?|Notes|
|---|---|---|---|---|
|69|UDP|To distribute images to devices using<br>TFTP.|Depends|Only if alternative protocols<br>like SCP or SFTP or HTTPS<br>are used for image distribution,<br>and if supported by the<br>managed devices.|
|162|UDP|To receive SNMP traps from network<br>devices.|No|—|
|443|TCP|For browser access to the Cisco EPN<br>Manager server via HTTPS.|No|—|
|514|UDP|To receive syslog messages from<br>network devices.|No|—|
|1522|TCP|For High Availability (HA)<br>communication between active and<br>standby Cisco EPN Manager servers.<br>Used to allow Oracle JDBC traffic for<br>Oracle database synchronization.|Yes|If at least one Cisco EPN<br>Manager server is not<br>configured for HA, this port is<br>automatically disabled.|
|2021|TCP|To distribute images to devices using<br>FTP.|No|—|
|6789|TCP|Used for Java Remote Method<br>Invocation (RMI) operations.|Yes|—|
|8005|TCP|Tomcat shutdown server socket port|Yes|—|
|8082|TCP|For the HA Health Monitor web<br>interface (via HTTPS).<br>Used by primary and secondary servers<br>to monitor their health status via<br>HTTPS.|No (If HA<br>configured)|—|
|8085|TCP|Used by the Health Monitor process to<br>check network bandwidth speed<br>between primary and secondary servers,<br>when the user executes readiness test<br>under high availability.|No (If HA<br>configured)|—|
|8087|TCP|To update software on the HA<br>secondary backup server (uses HTTPS<br>as transport).|No|—|
|8091|TCP|This port is used by the Web Container.|Yes|—|
|8456|TCP|It is used by Tomcat HTTP connector<br>for HTTP/1.1 requests.|Yes|—|

## Page 819

### p819_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Administer the Cisco EPN Manager System|Col2|
|---|---|
|**Generate and Apply a CA-Signed Web Server Certificate**||



### p819_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Signing<br>Entity|Description|See:|
|---|---|---|
|Certificate<br>Authority<br>(CA) signed<br>certificates|A Certificate Authority (CA) generates and issues these certificates. The<br>certificates bind a public key to the name of the entity (for example, a server<br>or device) that is identified in the certificate. You must generate a Certificate<br>Signing Request (CSR) file from the Cisco EPN Manager server, and submit<br>the CSR file (which contains the server key) to the CA. When you receive<br>the certificates, you apply them to the web server.<br>These certificates can be generated by an external CA or an internal CA.<br>• External CA—An external CA organization validates identities and<br>issues the certificates, usually for a fee. (Popular browsers are usually<br>pre-installed with Root and Intermediate certificates issued by the<br>external CA organization).<br>• Internal CA—Uses a certificate-generating server within your<br>organization (this avoids a fee). The internal CA functions exactly the<br>same way as an external fee-based CA.<br>This method can be used on:<br>• Deployments that do not use HA<br>• HA deployments that_ do_ use virtual IP addresses (including SSL<br>connections between browser-based clients)<br>**Note**<br>Depending on your deployment, you may need to instruct your users to<br>install the CA-signed Root and Intermediate certificates to their browser<br>or OS certificate store. Ask your organization's IT administrator if this is<br>required. Instructions are provided in Add the CA-Signed Root and<br>Intermediate Certificates to a Browser/OS Trust Store, on page 788.|Generate and<br>Apply a<br>CA-Signed Web<br>Server<br>Certificate, on<br>page 779|



### p819_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Deployment Type|Summary of Steps|
|---|---|
|Deployment without HA|For deployments without HA, you must request the certificate, import it into your<br>web server, and restart the web server to apply it, as described in these topics:<br>**1.**<br>Request a CA-Signed Web Server Certificate, on page 780<br>**2.**<br>Import and Apply a CA-Signed Web Server Certificate—No HA, on page<br>781|



### p819_default_t4 (default, high confidence)

|Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager 7.0 User and Administrator Guide|Col2|Col3|
|---|---|---|
|||**779**|



---

## Page 820

### p820_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Administer the Cisco EPN Manager System|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Request a CA-Signed Web Server Certificate**|



### p820_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Deployment Type|Summary of Steps|
|---|---|
|High availability<br>deployment_ not using_<br>virtual IP addresses|For HA deployments that do not use virtual IPs, you must request separate<br>certificates for the primary and secondary servers and then import the appropriate<br>certificate onto each server. When you restart the servers to apply the certificates,<br>you must restart them in a specific order. The entire procedure is described in<br>these topics:<br>**1.**<br>Request a CA-Signed Web Server Certificate, on page 780<br>**2.**<br>Import and Apply CA-Signed Web Server Certificates—HA Without Virtual<br>IP Addresses, on page 783|
|High availability<br>deployment_ using_ virtual<br>IP addresses|For HA deployments that use virtual IPs, you only need to request a single<br>certificate for both servers. You must remove HA on the servers, import the<br>certificate on both servers, and then restart the servers to apply the certificate<br>(you must restart the servers in a specific order). Finally, you reconfigure HA by<br>registering the secondary server on the primary server. The entire procedure is<br>described in these topics:<br>**1.**<br>Request, Import, and Apply a CA-Signed Web Server Certificate—HA With<br>Virtual IP Addresses, on page 785<br>**2.**<br>How to Configure HA Between the Primary and Secondary Servers, on page<br>918|



### p820_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Col1|Col2|Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager 7.0 User and Administrator Guide|
|---|---|---|
|**780**|||

### p856_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Administer the Cisco EPN Manager System|Col2|

||**User Interfaces and User Types**|



### p856_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Cisco EPN Manager<br>User Interface|Interface Description|CEPNM User Types|
|---|---|---|
|Cisco EPN Manager<br>web GUI|Web interface that facilitates day-to-day<br>and administration operations using the<br>web GUI. These users can have varying<br>degrees of privileges and are classified<br>into role-based access control (RBAC)<br>classes and subclasses.<br>This interface provides a subset of<br>operations that are provided by the Cisco<br>EPN Manager CLI admin and CLI config<br>users.|**Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager web GUI**<br>**everyday users**—Created by web GUI root user. These users<br>have varying degrees of privileges and are classified into<br>role-based access control (RBAC) classes and subclasses called<br>_user groups_ (Admin, Super Users, Config Managers, and so<br>forth). For information on the user groups, see Types of User<br>Groups, on page 819.<br>**Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager web GUI**<br>**root user**—Created at installation and intended for first-time<br>login to the web GUI, and for creating other user accounts. This<br>account should be disabled after creating at least one web GUI<br>user that has Admin privileges, that is, a web GUI user that<br>belongs to the Admin or Super Users user group. See Disable<br>and Enable the Web GUI root User, on page 818.<br>**Note**<br>The Cisco EPN Manager web GUI root user is not the same as<br>the Linux CLI root user, nor is it the same as the Cisco EPN<br>Manager CLI admin user.|
|North Bound Interface<br>(NBI) REST API|NBI is REST Application Programming<br>Interface that allows a client system to talk<br>to Cisco EPN Manager to carry out<br>day-to-day and administration operations.<br>Special privileged service account users<br>are assigned to a client system to allow<br>talking to Cisco EPN Manager using this<br>interface.<br>These NBI users can also have varying<br>degrees of privileges and are also<br>classified into role-based access control<br>(RBAC) classes and subclasses.|Cisco EPN Manager NBI users—Created by web GUI root user.<br>These users have three different types of privileges and are<br>classified into role-based access control (RBAC) classes and<br>subclasses called NBI user groups (NBI Read and NBI Write).<br>For information on the user groups, see section User<br>Groups—NBI, on page 820|



### p856_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Col1|Col2|Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager 7.0 User and Administrator Guide|
|---|---|---|
|**816**|||

## Page 857

### p857_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Administer the Cisco EPN Manager System|Col2|
|---|---|
|**How to Transition Between the CLI User Interfaces in Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager**||



### p857_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Cisco EPN Manager<br>User Interface|Interface Description|CEPNM User Types|
|---|---|---|
|CEPNM Admin CLI|Cisco proprietary shell which provides<br>secure and restricted access to the system<br>(as compared with the Linux shell). This<br>Admin shell and CLI provide commands<br>for advanced Cisco EPN Manager<br>administration tasks. These commands are<br>explained throughout this guide. To use<br>this CLI, you must have Cisco EPN<br>Manager CLI admin user access. You can<br>access this shell from a remote computer<br>using SSH.|**Cisco EPN Manager CLI Admin user**—Created at installation<br>time and used for administration operations such as stopping<br>and restarting the application and creating remote backup<br>repositories. (A subset of these administration operations is<br>available in the web GUI.)<br>To display a list of operations this user can perform, enter** ?** at<br>the prompt.<br>Some tasks must be performed in config mode. To transition to<br>config mode, use the procedure in Transition Between the Cisco<br>Evolved Programmable Network Manager admin CLI and Cisco<br>Evolved Programmable Network Manager config CLI, on page<br>817.<br>The admin CLI user can create other CLI users for various<br>reasons, using the following command:<br>`(config)`**` username`**_` username`_**` password role`**` {`**`admin`**`|`**`user`**`}`<br>_`password`_<br>These users may have admin-like privilege/roles or lower-level<br>privileges as defined during creation time. To create a Cisco<br>Evolved Programmable Network Manager CLI user with admin<br>privileges, run the** username** command with the** admin** keyword;<br>otherwise, use the** user** keyword. For password limitations, see<br>Create Admin User, on page 748.|
|CEPNM Config CLI|Cisco proprietary shell which is restricted<br>and more secure than the Linux shell. This<br>Config shell and CLI provide commands<br>for Cisco EPN Manager system<br>configuration tasks. These commands are<br>explained throughout this guide. To use<br>this CLI, you must have admin-level user<br>access (see the information in the User<br>Types column of this table). You can<br>access this shell in the Admin CLI shell.|Cisco proprietary shell which is restricted<br>and more secure than the Linux shell. This<br>Config shell and CLI provide commands<br>for Cisco EPN Manager system<br>configuration tasks. These commands are<br>explained throughout this guide. To use<br>this CLI, you must have admin-level user<br>access (see the information in the User<br>Types column of this table). You can<br>access this shell in the Admin CLI shell.|
|Linux CLI|Linux shell which provides all Linux<br>commands. The Linux shell should only<br>be used by Cisco technical support<br>representatives. Regular system<br>administrators should not use the Linux<br>shell. You cannot reach this shell from a<br>remote computer using SSH; you can only<br>reach it through the admin shell and CLI.|**Linux CLI admin user**—Created at installation time and used<br>for Linux-level administration purposes.|

|**Types of User Groups**||



### p859_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|User Group|Group Task Focus|
|---|---|
|Root|All operations. The group permissions are not editable. The root web UI user is available<br>after installation and is described in User Interfaces and User Types, on page 815. The<br>best practice is to create other users with Admin or Super Users privileges, and disable<br>the root web UI user as described in Disable and Enable the Web GUI root User, on<br>page 818.|
|Super Users|All operations (not by default). The group permissions are editable. Can enable<br>permissions similar to those of a root user.|
|Admin|Administer the system and server. Can also perform monitoring and configuration<br>operations. The group permissions are editable.|
|Config Managers|Configure and monitor the network (no administration tasks). The permissions assigned<br>to this group are editable.|
|System Monitoring|Monitor the network (no configuration tasks). The group permissions are editable.|
|Help Desk Admin|Only has access to the help desk and user preferences-related pages. This is a special<br>group which lacks access to the user interface.|

|Category selected under Notification Policy Page|Points to Remember|
|---|---|
|Notification Policy|• Each notification policy consists of the following<br>criteria: alarm categories, alarm severities, alarm<br>types, device groups, notification destinations,<br>and time range.<br>• While selecting the required conditions, you can<br>drill down the tree view drop-down list and select<br>the individual categories (for example, Switches<br>and Routers) and the severity (for example,<br>Major). You can further select the specific Alarm<br>types (for example, link down).<br>• Alarms that match the criteria in a policy are<br>forwarded to the respective notification<br>destinations.<br>• If an alarm is matched against multiple policies<br>and these policies have the same destinations,<br>only one notification is sent to each destination.<br>• If one or more device groups specified in a policy<br>is deleted, no alarm will match this policy.<br>Though, this notification policy will be listed in<br>the main Notification Policy page, you cannot<br>modify or view the details of this notification<br>policy. However, you can delete this policy.<br>• Alarms that are suppressed due to an existing<br>alarm policy will not be forwarded to the<br>notification destinations.<br>• If a notification policy that includes both system<br>and non-system category alarms in the rule<br>criteria, you must select the device group(s) for<br>the non-system category alarms.<br>• The alarms generated in the specified duration<br>alone are sent to the notification destination. For<br>example, if you specify the duration as 8:00 to<br>17:00, the alarms will be notified from 8.00 a.m.<br>to 5.00 p.m.|



### p917_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager 7.0 User and Administrator Guide|Col2|Col3|
|---|---|---|
|||**877**|

## Page 940

### p940_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Administer the Cisco EPN Manager System|Col2|
|---|---|
||**Adjust General Log File Settings and Default Sizes**|



### p940_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|To do the following:|From Administration > Settings > Logging:|
|---|---|
|Change the size of logs,<br>number of logs saved, and<br>the file compression<br>options|Adjust the Log File Settings.<br>**Note**<br>Change these settings with caution to avoid impacting the system. As per log4j<br>MaxBackupIndex, there will be one main file accompanied by the set number<br>of backup files. For example, if the number of log files is set to 3, there is one<br>main file (.log) and 3 backup files (.log.1, .log.2, and .log.3).<br>If the** Number of files** is modified to a value lower than the one previously set,<br>the log file settings are applied only to the newly generated files. For example,<br>if the preset value was 5 and now you modify it to 2, the settings will only be<br>applied to files .log, .log.1 and .log.2. There is no changes to the files .log.3,<br>.log.4, and .log.5.<br>If you select the** Compression (Zip)** option, log files are compressed and<br>archived in the folder of the process. Retention of the compressed log files is<br>subject to the criteria:<br>• Storage (MB): Maximum size of the folder in MB<br>• Number of Days: Maximum age of the log files<br>The purge is triggered when either of the criteria is met.<br>Optionally, if** Backup to external location** is enabled, log files marked for<br>cleanup are copied to the specified external repository prior to deletion.|
|Change the logging level<br>for specific modules/<br>microservices|In the General Log Settings, select the files and the desired level, and click** Save**.<br>For example, from the** Message Level** drop-down list, choose one of the<br>following as current logging level:<br>• Error—Captures error logs on the system.<br>• Information—Captures informational logs on the system.<br>• Trace—Reproduces problems of managed devices on the system so the<br>details can be captured in the logs.<br>• Debug—Captures debugging logs on the system.<br>When you restart Cisco EPN Manager , the log level resets to Error.|
|Download log files for<br>troubleshooting purposes|In the** Global Settings** tab, click** Download**.|

|NETWORK - CHECK NETWORK INTERFACE<br>BANDWIDTH|This checks if the eth0 interface speed matches the<br>recommended speed of 100 Mbps in both primary and<br>secondary server.<br>This test will not measure network bandwidth by<br>transmitting data between primary and secondary server.|
|NETWORK-CHECKNETWORKBANDWIDTHSPEED|This checks if the network bandwidth speed matches the<br>recommended speed of 100 Mbps in both primary and<br>secondary server.<br>This test measures the network bandwidth by transmitting<br>data between primary and secondary server.|
|DATABASE - CHECK ONLINE STATUS|This checks if the database files status is online and<br>accessible in both primary and secondary server.|
|DATABASE - CHECK TNS CONFIG CORRUPTION|This validates if the tnsping is successful in both primary<br>and secondary server.|
|DATABASE - TNS REACHABILITY STATUS|This checks if all the wcs instances exist under oracle<br>"listener.ora" file.<br>This is executable in both primary and secondary server.|

### p968_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|1|Settings—Displays the Health Monitor state and<br>configuration detail in five separate sections.|2|Status—Indicates the current functional status of<br>the HA setup (a green check mark indicates HA<br>is enabled and working).|
|---|---|---|---|
|3|Events—Displays the current HA-related events<br>in chronological order, with the most recent<br>events at the top.|4|Primary/Secondary IP address—Displays the<br>IP address of the paired servers. Because this<br>Health Monitor instance is running on the<br>secondary server, it shows the IP address of the<br>primary server.|
|5|Download—Lets you download the Health<br>Monitor log files.|6|State—Shows the current state of the server on<br>which this Health Monitor instance is running (in<br>this case, the secondary server).|
|7|Message Level—Indicates the current logging<br>level, which you can change (Error,<br>Informational, or Trace). You must click** Save**<br>to change the logging level.|8|Title bar—Identifies the HA server whose Health<br>Monitor web page you are viewing, along with<br>the Refresh and Logout buttons. Note that the<br>Software Update is only displayed for secondary<br>servers.|
|9|Failover Type—Shows whether you have<br>Manual or Automatic failover configured.|10|Action—Shows the actions you can perform, such<br>as failover or failback. Only the available actions<br>are displayed here.|
|11|Check Failover Readiness—Shows the outcome<br>of the disk speed, network interface bandwidth<br>and DB sync status checks after the HA<br>configuration is enabled.|||
