## Page 984

### p984_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Administer the Cisco EPN Manager System|Col2|
|---|---|
||**HA Configuration Modes**|



### p984_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Mode|Description|
|---|---|
|HA Not Configured|HA is not configured on this server.|
|HA Initializing|HA configuration process between the primary and secondary servers has started.|
|HA Enabled|HA is enabled between the primary and secondary servers.|
|HA Alone|Server is running alone because one of the servers is down, out of sync, or unreachable.|



### p984_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|State|Server|Description|
|---|---|---|
|Stand Alone|Both|HA is not configured on this server.|
|Primary Alone|Primary|Primary server has restarted after it lost the secondary server (only<br>Health Monitor is running in this state).|
|HA Initializing|Both|HA configuration process between the primary and secondary server<br>has started.|
|Primary Active|Primary|Primary server is now active and is synchronizing with the<br>secondary server.|
|Primary Database<br>Copy Failed|Primary|Restarted primary server detected a data gap, triggered a data copy<br>from the active secondary server, and the database copy failed.<br>When a primary server is restarted, it always checks to see if a data<br>gap has occurred due to the primary server being down for 24 hours<br>or more. This copy rarely fails but if it occurs, all attempts to<br>failback to the primary are blocked until the database copy<br>completes successfully. As soon as it does, the primary state is set<br>to** Primary Syncing**.|
|Primary Failover|Primary|Primary server detected a failure.|
|Primary Failback|Primary|User-triggered failback is currently in progress.|
|Primary Lost<br>Secondary|Primary|Primary server is unable to communicate with the secondary server.|



### p984_default_t4 (default, high confidence)

|Col1|Col2|Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager 7.0 User and Administrator Guide|
|---|---|---|
|**944**|||



---

## Page 985

### p985_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Administer the Cisco EPN Manager System|Col2|
|---|---|
|**HA States and Transitions**||



### p985_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Primary Preparing<br>for Failback|Primary|Primary server has started up in standby mode after a failover<br>(because the secondary server is still active). When the primary<br>server is ready for failback, its state will be set to Primary Syncing.|
|---|---|---|
|Primary Syncing|Primary|Primary server is synchronizing the database and configuration<br>files from the active secondary server. This occurs after a failover,<br>when primary processes are brought up (and the secondary server<br>is playing the active role).|
|Primary Uncertain|Primary|Primary server's application processes are not able to connect to<br>its database.|
|Secondary Alone|Secondary|Primary server is not reachable from secondary server after a<br>primary server restart.|
|Secondary Syncing|Secondary|Secondary server is synchronizing the database and configuration<br>files from the primary server.|
|Secondary Active|Secondary|Failover from the primary server to the secondary server has<br>completed successfully.|
|Secondary Lost<br>Primary|Secondary|Secondary server is not able to connect to the primary server (occurs<br>when the primary fails or network connectivity is lost).<br>For automatic failover, the secondary server will automatically<br>move to the** Secondary Active** state. For Manual failover, you<br>must trigger the failover to make the secondary server active (see<br>Trigger Failover, on page 930).|
|Secondary Failover|Secondary|Failover triggered and is in progress.|
|Secondary Failback|Secondary|Failback triggered and database and file replication is in progress.|
|Secondary Post<br>Failback|Secondary|Failback triggered; associated process stops and restarts are in<br>progress. Database and configuration files have been replicated<br>from the secondary server to the primary server. The primary server<br>status will change to** Primary Active**, and the secondary server<br>HA status will change to** Secondary Syncing**.|
|Secondary<br>Uncertain|Secondary|Secondary server's application processes cannot connect to the<br>server's database.|



### p985_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager 7.0 User and Administrator Guide|Col2|Col3|

## Page 1001

### p1001_default_t1 (default, high confidence)

|Icon|Device<br>Reachability<br>State|Description|Troubleshooting|
|---|---|---|---|
||Reachable|Cisco EPN Manager can<br>reach the device using<br>SNMP, or the NCS 2K<br>device using ICMP.|—|
||Ping<br>reachable|Cisco EPN Manager can<br>reach the device using<br>Ping, but not via SNMP.|Although ICMP ping is successful, check for all possible<br>reasons why SNMP communication is failing. Check<br>that device SNMP credentials are the same in both the<br>device and in Cisco EPN Manager, whether SNMP is<br>enabled on the device, or whether the transport network<br>is dropping SNMP packets due to reasons such as<br>mis-configuration, etc. See Change Basic Device<br>Properties, on page 324.|

### p1002_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Col1|Unreachable|Cisco EPN Manager<br>cannot reach the device<br>using Ping.|Verify that the physical device is operational and<br>connected to the network.|
|---|---|---|---|
||Unknown|Cisco EPN Manager<br>cannot connect to the<br>device.|Check the device.|



### p1002_default_t3 (default, high confidence)

|Device Admin<br>State|Description|Troubleshooting|
|---|---|---|
|Managed|Cisco EPN Manager is<br>actively monitoring the<br>device.|Not Applicable.|
|Maintenance|Cisco EPN Manager is<br>checking the device for<br>reachability but is not<br>processing traps, syslogs,<br>or TL1 messages.|To move a device back to Managed state, see Move a Device<br>To and From Maintenance State, on page 67.|
|Unmanaged|Cisco EPN Manager is not<br>monitoring the device.|In the Network Devices table, locate the device and click the<br>"i" icon next to the data in the** Last Inventory Collection**<br>**Status** column. The popup window will provide details and<br>troubleshooting tips. Typical reasons for collection problems<br>are:<br>• Device SNMP credentials are incorrect.<br>• The Cisco EPN Manager deployment has exceeded the<br>number of devices allowed by its license.<br>• A device is enabled for switch path tracing only.<br>If a device type is not supported, its Device Type will be<br>**Unknown**. You can check if support for that device type is<br>available from Cisco.com by choosing** Administration** ><br>**Licenses and Software Updates** >** Software Update** and then<br>clicking** Check for Updates**.|
|Unknown|Cisco EPN Manager<br>cannot connect to the<br>device.|Check the device.|

### p1006_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Auto Up|Col2|Circuit or VC is operationally auto up and administratively up. Only certain<br>devices support the Auto Up operational state.|
|---|---|---|

|Partial||Circuit/VC operational or administrative state is partial.<br>• Partial admin state—The circuit or VC has a mixed administrative<br>request (to activate some service resources and deactivate others), has<br>a mix of resources that are administratively up and down, or has<br>resources whose operational state is unavailable.<br>• Partial operational state—The circuit or VC has a mix of some active<br>and deactivated resources, or the operational state for some of its<br>resources are unavailable.|
|Up -<br>Unprotected||The circuit/VC that was configured with a protection path is operational but<br>cannot switch to the alternate path because of severe failures.<br>**Note**<br>This serviceability status indication is supported for OCHCC WSON circuits<br>with Y-Cable protection and protected ODU.|

### p1011_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|---|---|---|

|---|---|---|

|Failed||Action has failed.|
|In Progress||Action was initiated but not yet completed.|
|Planned||Action is planned but not yet initiated.|
|Succeeded||Action has completed successfully.|

|---|---|---|
|Admin Down||Link was purposefully shut down by the administrator.|
|Down||Link is down (but it should not be).|
|Up||Link is up and traffic is passing through the link.|
|Auto Up||Link is up because it detected a signal (this state is only supported by optical<br>devices).|
|Unavailable||Link is not discovered yet or its status is unavailable.|

|ifOutMulticastPkts|The total number of multicast frames transmitted error free.|
|ifInBroadcastPkts|The total number of broadcast packets received since the last counter reset.|
|ifOutBroadcastPkts|The total number of packets requested by higher-level protocols and addressed<br>to a broadcast address at this sublayer, including those that were not<br>transmitted.|
|txTotalPkts|The total number of packets transmitted.|
|rxTotalPkts|The total number of packets received.|
|etherStatsOctets|The total number of octets of data (including those in bad packets) received<br>on the network (excluding framing bits but including FCS octets).|
|etherStatsOversizePkts|The total number of packets received that were longer than 1518 octets<br>(excluding framing bits but including FCS octets) and were otherwise well<br>formed. Note that for tagged interfaces, this number becomes 1522 bytes.|
|dot3StatsFCSErrors|A count of frames received on a particular interface that are an integral number<br>of octets in length but do not pass the FCS check.|
|dot3StatsFrameTooLongs|A count of frames received on a particular interface that exceed the maximum<br>permitted frame size.|

### p1042_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|MS-EB|Number of errored block per multiplex section for near end and far end devices.|
|---|---|
|MS-FC|Number of failure counts per multiplex section for near end and far end devices.|
|MS-PSC|Protection switching count per multiplex section. PSC is the number of times the service<br>switches from a working card to a protection card and back.|
|MS-PSC-R|Protection switching count ring per multiplex section. This count is incremented only<br>if ring switching is used.|
|MS-PSC-S|Protection switching count span per multiplex section. This count is incremented only<br>if span switching is used.|
|MS-PSC-W|Protection switching count working per multiplex section. It is the count of the number<br>of times traffic switches away from the working capacity in the failed line and back to<br>the working capacity after the failure is cleared. PSC-W increments on the failed working<br>line.|
|MS-PSD|Protection switching duration applies to the length of time, in seconds, that service is<br>carried on another line.|
|MS-PSD-R|Protection switching duration ring is a count of the seconds that the protection line was<br>used to carry service. This count is incremented only if ring switching is used.|
|MS-PSD-S|Protection switching duration span is a count of the seconds that the protection line was<br>used to carry service. This count is incremented only if span switching is used.|
|MS-PSD-W|Protection switching duration working per multiplex section.|
|RS-ES|Number of errored seconds per regenerator section.|
|RS-ESR|Errored seconds ratio per regenerator section.|
|RS-SES|Number of severely errored seconds per regenerator section.|
|RS-SESR|Severely errored seconds ratio per regenerator section.|
|RS-BBE|Number of background block errors per regenerator section.|
|RS-BBER|Background block errors ratio per regenerator section.|
|RS-UAS|Number of unavailable seconds per regenerator section.|

||**Cisco Evolved Programmable Network Manager RESTful API**|



### p1052_default_t2 (default, high confidence)

|Query Parameter|Applicability|Meaning|
|---|---|---|
|.group|api/v1/data/T|Filters the response based on<br>content of the group specified by<br>the string value, and the result of<br>any applied operator.|
|.transform|GET/POST|Supplies the logical-name of a<br>transform to be applied<br>immediately before rendering to<br>XML or JSON.|
|.maxresults|GET Paged|The greatest number of results in<br>terms of the heads of instance trees<br>returned.|
|.firstResult|GET Paged|The first result in terms of the heads<br>of instance trees.|
|.strict|/api/v1/data/T|When ‘true’, the property names<br>used in queries are validated, and<br>an error thrown if appropriate. (The<br>default - that is, when strict=false -<br>is to ignore invalid property names<br>with a simple log message.)|
|.case_sensitve|/api/v1/data/T|When ‘true’, the string values used<br>in filter queries are case sensitive.<br>(The default - ie when<br>.case_sensitive=false - is to treat<br>comparisons as case insensitive).|
|.nocount|/api/v1/data/T|When ‘true’, the “count”, “first”,<br>and “last” attributes are not<br>included the response. Getting the<br>values of these attributes requires<br>additional time, therefore setting<br>this to ‘true’ will improve<br>performance. Defaults to ‘false’.|
|_ctx.domain|GET|Sets the active domain to be that<br>named in the query parameter value<br>- this is, by default, “sticky” in the<br>sense that once set, the<br>active-domain remains set. The<br>“stickiness” is not RESTful, and so<br>it can be switched off in<br>configuration.|
